Divine Decree
beginner
4 min
Refutation from Command and Prohibition
Maturidi argues from the nature of command and prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine commands inherently imply real human ability to act, refuting the claim that all actions are directly compelled by God.

Core Idea
Commands without ability are meaningless, so human action must be real.

Maturidi begins his refutation of Jabr by focusing on the very nature of divine command. If humans had no true agency, God's commands would be absurd—like commanding yesterday's events. This argument grounds the debate in the logic of language and divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the logical flow: premise (God commands), impossibility (command without action), Quranic support, and absurd hypothetical.
The verse 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence' anchors the argument.
2
Identify the core logical premise
The key premise is that commanding something presupposes the ability of the commanded to perform it. If not, the command is meaningless.
Think about the difference between a command and a description.
3
Consider the absurd hypothetical
Maturidi uses a strong reductio: if commands didn't require real action, one could command events of the past or the creation of the universe. This shows the absurdity of the Jabr view.
This highlights that Jabr leads to contradictions in the very concept of command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمال، ولأفعالهم أسماء الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله سبحانه نفي ذلك، بل هي الله بأن خلقها على ما هي عليه، وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها. على أن الله إذ أمر ونهى، ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل فيه للمأمور أو المنهى، قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّ اللهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالإِحْسَانِ"، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز اليوم الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بانشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق. ثم في العقل قبيح إن انضاف إلى الله الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير وأنه المأمور والمنهى والمثاب والمعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا إن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزى بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وكذلك في أنه محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعها أو يعصيها، ومحال تسمية الله عبدا ذليلا مطيعا عاصيا سفيها جائرا، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم. فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق، ولا غير ثمة، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن كل أحد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب، فلو جاز صرف مثله مما طريق العلم به الحس، وإبطاله نحو العلم لجميع العالم مثله، وذلك مهجور، فمثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول يغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه؛ لما ليس له كثير اتباع، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه؛ إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج فزال الذي به يكون الحجاج واضمحل.
And other than that which established for them names of workers, and for their actions names of action by command and prohibition and promise and threat, and not in the attribution to God, Exalted is He, is negation of that, but rather it is God by creating them as they are, and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for creation according to what they earned and did. Moreover, when God commands and prohibits, it is impossible to command what has no action for the commanded or prohibited; God said: 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence'; and if it were permissible to command that without meaning of action in reality, it would be permissible today to command something that would be for yesterday or last year or for creating creatures, even though there is no meaning for that in the matter of creation. Then, in the intellect, it is ugly if obedience and disobedience and committing indecencies and abominations are attributed to God, and that He is the commanded and the prohibited and the rewarded and the punished; so the action is invalidated from being from Him in these respects, and there is no power except by Allah. And also, God only promised reward to those who obey Him in this world and punishment to those who disobey Him; so if both matters are His action, then He is the one who recompenses as mentioned, and if reward and punishment are a reality, then compliance and avoidance are likewise, and there is no power except by Allah. And likewise, it is impossible that one command himself or obey himself or disobey himself, and it is impossible to name God as a humble servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, oppressor, while God named with all this those whom He commanded and prohibited. So if these names become in reality for Him, then He would be the Lord and the servant, the Creator and the created, and there is no other, and that is rejected by scripture and reason, and there is no power except by Allah. And also, everyone knows from himself that he is free in what he does, and that he is an agent, a gainer; so if it were permissible to turn such a thing whose way of knowledge is sense, and its invalidation would be like the knowledge of the entire world similarly, that is abandoned; so its like is the saying of the people of compulsion (jabr), and this is a saying that makes the narrative dispense with elaboration; because it has no many followers, and because this saying has no meaning for its speaker to discuss; since it denies from itself the reality of every saying and action, and when it is denied, the saying is invalid, and by it one argues and debates, so that by which debate occurs vanishes and disappears.
Source pages p. 825

Commentary
This passage contains Maturidi's refutation of the Jabriyya (compulsionist) doctrine, which holds that all human actions are directly created by God with no human agency. The proof proceeds through several arguments:

1. **Argument from Command and Prohibition**: If humans have no real action, then God's commands and prohibitions would be meaningless, since commanding presupposes the ability to obey or disobey. Maturidi quotes the Quranic verse on justice and excellence to show that command is real, and if it were not, one could command things of the past. This is absurd, so humans must have real action.

2. **Argument from Moral Ugliness**: Attributing obedience, disobedience, and indecencies to God is intellectually repugnant. If God were both the commander and the actor in all actions, He would be subject to His own commands, which is impossible. Therefore, actions cannot be solely from God.

3. **Argument from Reward and Punishment**: God promises reward and punishment based on human actions. If both reward and punishment are God's own acts, then He would be rewarding and punishing Himself. But reward and punishment are real, so the actions that elicit them must also be real human actions.

4. **Argument from the Impossibility of Self-Command**: It is impossible for one to command, obey, or disobey oneself. God calls certain people 'servants', 'obedient', 'disobedient', etc. If He were the sole agent, He would be called by all these names, which is absurd and rejected by scripture and reason.

5. **Argument from Self-Awareness**: Every person knows directly that they are free and are agents who earn their actions. To deny this is to deny sensory knowledge, which would undermine all knowledge. The claim of the Jabriyya is self-defeating because it denies the very reality of speech and action, making debate impossible.

Maturidi concludes that the Jabriyya position is baseless and lacks followers, and its denial of reality renders it incoherent.

Key Terms
الأمر
النهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That divine commands are merely declarative and do not require human ability to obey.
Correction: Commands inherently imply the ability to perform the commanded act; otherwise they would be absurd, as shown by the impossibility of commanding past events.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi argue would be possible if commands did not require real action?
A) Commanding the creation of the universe
B) Commanding only good deeds
C) Commanding without any language
D) Commanding angels

Key Takeaway
Divine commands are proof that humans have real agency, otherwise the commands would be meaningless and absurd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fail to obey a clear command of Allah, do you truly believe you had the ability to obey? How does this lesson expose the excuses you make for your disobedience?
?
This lesson proves that Allah's commands are meaningful only if you have real agency. In what specific area of your life are you acting as if you have no control, and how will you take responsibility starting today?
?
If commands without ability are impossible, then every command Allah gives you is a reminder of your capacity to act. Will you now treat every divine command as a call to real action, or will you continue to live as if you are powerless?

Divine Decree

3 min
Refutation from Moral Ugliness
Maturidi argues from the intellectual ugliness of attributing sin to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing disobedience and indecencies to God is intellectually repugnant, thereby refuting the Jabriyya claim that all actions are from God.

Core Idea
If God caused all actions, He would be responsible for evil, which is absurd.

Maturidi now turns to a rational argument: it is intellectually repugnant to attribute obedience, disobedience, and immoral acts to God. If God were the sole agent, He would be both the commander and the subject of His own commands, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the terms 'qabih' (ugly) and how Maturidi lists the consequences.
The argument relies on innate moral intuition.
2
Understand the repugnance
Maturidi says it is 'qabih' (ugly in the intellect) to attribute obedience, disobedience, and immoral acts to God. God is above such things.
This is not just an emotional reaction but a rational judgment.
3
See the logical conclusion
If God were the doer of all actions, then He would be the one commanded, prohibited, rewarded, and punished—which is impossible. Therefore, actions cannot be solely from God.
This shows the Jabr view leads to a conceptual contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's creation of all actions does not make Him responsible for evil because He creates it for a purpose.
Correction: Maturidi argues that attributing obedience and disobedience to God is rationally ugly, regardless of purpose, because it implies God is subject to His own commands.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is 'qabih' (ugly) to attribute to God?
A) Power and mercy
B) Obedience and disobedience
C) Creation and sustenance
D) Commanding only good

Key Takeaway
Attributing moral evil to God is intellectually repugnant, proving that humans are the real agents of their actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly take full responsibility for your action, or do you subtly blame your circumstances or even God? How does Maturidi's argument force you to own your choices?
?
If you genuinely believed that God is not the creator of your evil deeds, would it change the way you repent? Would it make your repentance more sincere and humble, knowing you alone are accountable?
?
How does the reality that God is too transcendent and pure to be associated with sin affect your relationship with Him? Does it draw you closer in awe and gratitude, or do you find yourself trying to distance yourself from your own sinfulness?

Refutation from Reward and Punishment
Maturidi argues from the reality of divine reward and punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the reality of divine reward and punishment presupposes genuine human agency, refuting Jabr.

Core Idea
If God caused all actions, He would reward and punish Himself, which is absurd.

Maturidi continues his multi-pronged refutation by focusing on the nature of reward and punishment. God promises reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience. If all actions were God's, then He would be rewarding and punishing Himself, which contradicts the very meaning of these terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and its translation. Note the parallel structure: reward/punishment are real, so the acts that elicit them must be real too.
The argument uses the principle of reciprocity.
2
Identify the key logical equivalence
Maturidi states: if reward and punishment are real, then 'compliance and avoidance' (i.e., the human responses) must also be real. This is because reward/punishment are based on these actions.
Think about the relationship between an action and its consequence.
3
See the reductio
If both reward and punishment were God's direct acts, then He would be the one being rewarded and punished—which is impossible. Therefore, the actions that earn reward/punishment must be human.
This argument is concise but powerful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمال، ولأفعالهم أسماء الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله سبحانه نفي ذلك، بل هي الله بأن خلقها على ما هي عليه، وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها. على أن الله إذ أمر ونهى، ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل فيه للمأمور أو المنهى، قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّ اللهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالإِحْسَانِ"، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز اليوم الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بانشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق. ثم في العقل قبيح إن انضاف إلى الله الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير وأنه المأمور والمنهى والمثاب والمعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا إن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزى بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وكذلك في أنه محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعها أو يعصيها، ومحال تسمية الله عبدا ذليلا مطيعا عاصيا سفيها جائرا، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم. فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق، ولا غير ثمة، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن كل أحد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب، فلو جاز صرف مثله مما طريق العلم به الحس، وإبطاله نحو العلم لجميع العالم مثله، وذلك مهجور، فمثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول يغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه؛ لما ليس له كثير اتباع، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه؛ إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج فزال الذي به يكون الحجاج واضمحل.
And other than that which established for them names of workers, and for their actions names of action by command and prohibition and promise and threat, and not in the attribution to God, Exalted is He, is negation of that, but rather it is God by creating them as they are, and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for creation according to what they earned and did. Moreover, when God commands and prohibits, it is impossible to command what has no action for the commanded or prohibited; God said: 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence'; and if it were permissible to command that without meaning of action in reality, it would be permissible today to command something that would be for yesterday or last year or for creating creatures, even though there is no meaning for that in the matter of creation. Then, in the intellect, it is ugly if obedience and disobedience and committing indecencies and abominations are attributed to God, and that He is the commanded and the prohibited and the rewarded and the punished; so the action is invalidated from being from Him in these respects, and there is no power except by Allah. And also, God only promised reward to those who obey Him in this world and punishment to those who disobey Him; so if both matters are His action, then He is the one who recompenses as mentioned, and if reward and punishment are a reality, then compliance and avoidance are likewise, and there is no power except by Allah. And likewise, it is impossible that one command himself or obey himself or disobey himself, and it is impossible to name God as a humble servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, oppressor, while God named with all this those whom He commanded and prohibited. So if these names become in reality for Him, then He would be the Lord and the servant, the Creator and the created, and there is no other, and that is rejected by scripture and reason, and there is no power except by Allah. And also, everyone knows from himself that he is free in what he does, and that he is an agent, a gainer; so if it were permissible to turn such a thing whose way of knowledge is sense, and its invalidation would be like the knowledge of the entire world similarly, that is abandoned; so its like is the saying of the people of compulsion (jabr), and this is a saying that makes the narrative dispense with elaboration; because it has no many followers, and because this saying has no meaning for its speaker to discuss; since it denies from itself the reality of every saying and action, and when it is denied, the saying is invalid, and by it one argues and debates, so that by which debate occurs vanishes and disappears.
Source pages p. 825

Commentary
This passage contains Maturidi's refutation of the Jabriyya (compulsionist) doctrine, which holds that all human actions are directly created by God with no human agency. The proof proceeds through several arguments:

1. **Argument from Command and Prohibition**: If humans have no real action, then God's commands and prohibitions would be meaningless, since commanding presupposes the ability to obey or disobey. Maturidi quotes the Quranic verse on justice and excellence to show that command is real, and if it were not, one could command things of the past. This is absurd, so humans must have real action.

2. **Argument from Moral Ugliness**: Attributing obedience, disobedience, and indecencies to God is intellectually repugnant. If God were both the commander and the actor in all actions, He would be subject to His own commands, which is impossible. Therefore, actions cannot be solely from God.

3. **Argument from Reward and Punishment**: God promises reward and punishment based on human actions. If both reward and punishment are God's own acts, then He would be rewarding and punishing Himself. But reward and punishment are real, so the actions that elicit them must also be real human actions.

4. **Argument from the Impossibility of Self-Command**: It is impossible for one to command, obey, or disobey oneself. God calls certain people 'servants', 'obedient', 'disobedient', etc. If He were the sole agent, He would be called by all these names, which is absurd and rejected by scripture and reason.

5. **Argument from Self-Awareness**: Every person knows directly that they are free and are agents who earn their actions. To deny this is to deny sensory knowledge, which would undermine all knowledge. The claim of the Jabriyya is self-defeating because it denies the very reality of speech and action, making debate impossible.

Maturidi concludes that the Jabriyya position is baseless and lacks followers, and its denial of reality renders it incoherent.

Key Terms
الثواب
العقاب
الائتمار
الانتهاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That reward and punishment are merely symbolic or that God creates them directly without human actions being real.
Correction: Maturidi shows that for reward and punishment to be meaningful, the human actions they reward or punish must also be real and attributed to humans.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi conclude from the reality of reward and punishment?
A) That God is just
B) That compliance and avoidance are also real
C) That all actions are from God
D) That reward is greater than punishment

Key Takeaway
The reality of reward and punishment necessarily implies real human actions of obedience and disobedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever attribute your sins to fate or God's will as an excuse? How does this passage collapse that excuse and place the weight of your choices back on you?
?
If you truly believed that your obedience and disobedience are your own real actions—not just something that happens to you—would you change how you approach your daily prayers and fasts?
?
When you sin, do you feel the personal accountability that this argument demands, or do you passively assume God's mercy without engaging your will? What one action will you take today to own your obedience?

Refutation from Impossibility of Self-Command
Maturidi argues from the impossibility of self-command and divine names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is impossible for God to command Himself, and why attributing servanthood to God is absurd, thereby refuting Jabr.

Core Idea
If God caused all actions, He would be both Lord and servant, which is contradictory.

Maturidi now uses a linguistic and conceptual argument: it is impossible for a person to command, obey, or disobey themselves. Similarly, it is absurd to call God a servant, disobedient, foolish, or oppressive. Yet the Quran applies such terms to humans, showing they are real agents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the list of names: humble servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, oppressor. These are applied to humans in the Quran.
The argument uses the principle that language must reflect reality.
2
Understand the impossibility of self-command
Maturidi states it is impossible (muhaal) for one to command oneself or obey/disobey oneself. This is a logical truth.
This applies to God as well: He cannot be subject to His own commands.
3
See the reductio result
If God were the sole agent, then all these names (servant, etc.) would apply to Him, which is rejected by scripture and reason. Therefore, humans must be real agents.
The conclusion is that the Jabr view leads to theological absurdity.

And other than that which established for them names of workers, and for their actions names of action by command and prohibition and promise and threat, and not in the attribution to God, Exalted is He, is negation of that, but rather it is God by creating them as they are, and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for creation according to what they earned and did. Refutation from Self-Awareness and Free Will
Maturidi argues from self-awareness and the self-refuting nature of Jabr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the innate human awareness of free will and choice serves as a direct refutation of Jabr, and why the Jabriyya position is self-defeating.

Core Idea
Everyone knows they are free; denying this destroys all knowledge.

In his final argument, Maturidi appeals to immediate self-knowledge: every person knows intuitively that they are free agents who earn their actions. To deny this is to deny sensory knowledge, which would undermine all human knowledge. The Jabriyya stance is also self-defeating because it denies the reality of speech and debate itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the emphasis on 'everyone knows from himself' and the conclusion that the Jabr position is self-refuting.
This is a epistemological argument based on necessary knowledge (al-'ilm al-daruri).
2
Understand the self-awareness argument
Maturidi says every person knows they are free (mukhtar) and that they are agents who earn actions. This is direct knowledge, not inferred.
This knowledge is so certain that denying it would lead to universal skepticism.
3
See the self-refuting nature of Jabr
The Jabriyya claim denies the reality of speech and action, which means their own debate is meaningless. If all actions are from God, then their argument itself is from God, so it cannot be a valid refutation.
This is a powerful logical blow: the position destroys its own grounds.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمال، ولأفعالهم أسماء الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله سبحانه نفي ذلك، بل هي الله بأن خلقها على ما هي عليه، وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها. على أن الله إذ أمر ونهى، ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل فيه للمأمور أو المنهى، قال الله تعالى: "إِنَّ اللهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالإِحْسَانِ"، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز اليوم الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بانشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق. ثم في العقل قبيح إن انضاف إلى الله الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير وأنه المأمور والمنهى والمثاب والمعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا إن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزى بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وكذلك في أنه محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعها أو يعصيها، ومحال تسمية الله عبدا ذليلا مطيعا عاصيا سفيها جائرا، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم. فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق، ولا غير ثمة، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن كل أحد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب، فلو جاز صرف مثله مما طريق العلم به الحس، وإبطاله نحو العلم لجميع العالم مثله، وذلك مهجور، فمثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول يغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه؛ لما ليس له كثير اتباع، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه؛ إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج فزال الذي به يكون الحجاج واضمحل.
And other than that which established for them names of workers, and for their actions names of action by command and prohibition and promise and threat, and not in the attribution to God, Exalted is He, is negation of that, but rather it is God by creating them as they are, and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for creation according to what they earned and did. Moreover, when God commands and prohibits, it is impossible to command what has no action for the commanded or prohibited; God said: 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence'; and if it were permissible to command that without meaning of action in reality, it would be permissible today to command something that would be for yesterday or last year or for creating creatures, even though there is no meaning for that in the matter of creation. Then, in the intellect, it is ugly if obedience and disobedience and committing indecencies and abominations are attributed to God, and that He is the commanded and the prohibited and the rewarded and the punished; so the action is invalidated from being from Him in these respects, and there is no power except by Allah. And also, God only promised reward to those who obey Him in this world and punishment to those who disobey Him; so if both matters are His action, then He is the one who recompenses as mentioned, and if reward and punishment are a reality, then compliance and avoidance are likewise, and there is no power except by Allah. And likewise, it is impossible that one command himself or obey himself or disobey himself, and it is impossible to name God as a humble servant, obedient, disobedient, foolish, oppressor, while God named with all this those whom He commanded and prohibited. So if these names become in reality for Him, then He would be the Lord and the servant, the Creator and the created, and there is no other, and that is rejected by scripture and reason, and there is no power except by Allah. And also, everyone knows from himself that he is free in what he does, and that he is an agent, a gainer; so if it were permissible to turn such a thing whose way of knowledge is sense, and its invalidation would be like the knowledge of the entire world similarly, that is abandoned; so its like is the saying of the people of compulsion (jabr), and this is a saying that makes the narrative dispense with elaboration; because it has no many followers, and because this saying has no meaning for its speaker to discuss; since it denies from itself the reality of every saying and action, and when it is denied, the saying is invalid, and by it one argues and debates, so that by which debate occurs vanishes and disappears.
Source pages p. 825

Commentary
This passage contains Maturidi's refutation of the Jabriyya (compulsionist) doctrine, which holds that all human actions are directly created by God with no human agency. The proof proceeds through several arguments:

1. **Argument from Command and Prohibition**: If humans have no real action, then God's commands and prohibitions would be meaningless, since commanding presupposes the ability to obey or disobey. Maturidi quotes the Quranic verse on justice and excellence to show that command is real, and if it were not, one could command things of the past. This is absurd, so humans must have real action.

2. **Argument from Moral Ugliness**: Attributing obedience, disobedience, and indecencies to God is intellectually repugnant. If God were both the commander and the actor in all actions, He would be subject to His own commands, which is impossible. Therefore, actions cannot be solely from God.

3. **Argument from Reward and Punishment**: God promises reward and punishment based on human actions. If both reward and punishment are God's own acts, then He would be rewarding and punishing Himself. But reward and punishment are real, so the actions that elicit them must also be real human actions.

4. **Argument from the Impossibility of Self-Command**: It is impossible for one to command, obey, or disobey oneself. God calls certain people 'servants', 'obedient', 'disobedient', etc. If He were the sole agent, He would be called by all these names, which is absurd and rejected by scripture and reason.

5. **Argument from Self-Awareness**: Every person knows directly that they are free and are agents who earn their actions. To deny this is to deny sensory knowledge, which would undermine all knowledge. The claim of the Jabriyya is self-defeating because it denies the very reality of speech and action, making debate impossible.

Maturidi concludes that the Jabriyya position is baseless and lacks followers, and its denial of reality renders it incoherent.

Key Terms
العلم الضروري
الاختيار
الفاعل الكاسب
الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That free will is merely an illusion or that sensory knowledge can be mistaken.
Correction: Maturidi treats the knowledge of free will as certain and undeniable; rejecting it leads to total skepticism, which is impractical and self-defeating.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does every person know from themselves?
A) That they are compelled by God
B) That they are free in what they do and are agents
C) That they have no real choice
D) That they are merely passive recipients

Key Takeaway
The innate human awareness of free will is a direct and certain refutation of Jabr, and the Jabr position itself is self-refuting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever made an excuse for a sin by saying 'It was written for me' or 'God made me do it'? If so, how does Maturidi's argument from self-awareness confront that excuse? Will you now take full responsibility for your choices?
?
When you argue with yourself over a difficult decision, do you sense that you are truly free to choose? If you deny that feeling, then by what basis do you even make the argument? Your own argument would vanish. Are you ready to live as someone who really has that choice?
?
The Jabr position, Maturidi says, has no meaning for its speaker to discuss. Have you ever held a belief that, upon reflection, undermines its own assertion? If your own deeply held convictions collapsed if followed to their logical end, would you have the courage to abandon them?

Two Erroneous Responses to Jabriyya and Divine Attribution
Maturidi discusses two groups that erred: those denying necessary knowledge and those affirming actions but negating creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two erroneous groups that emerged in response to Jabriyya: those who denied necessary knowledge and those who affirmed human actions but negated God's creation and management, and the two ways they proposed to attribute actions to God.

Core Idea
Response to Jabriyya can go wrong by either denying necessary knowledge or by denying God's management and creation of actions.

Maturidi continues his discussion on human action by addressing alternative views that arose in reaction to the determinist (Jabriyya) position. Some opponents went too far by claiming similarity between God and creation, while others affirmed human actions but stripped God of any real creative involvement. This passage critiques both errors and presents the nuanced ways these thinkers attempted to attribute actions to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
The passage is dense with theological terminology; the translation will help clarify.
2
Identify the two groups and their errors
Notice that the first group is dismissed for denying necessary knowledge, while the second group affirms human acts but negates God's creation and management. Understand why both are problematic according to Maturidi.
The second group uses command and prohibition verses to argue, but Maturidi hints their position is flawed.
3
Examine the two modes of attribution
The second group proposes two ways to attribute actions to God aside from direct creation: attribution by cause and attribution at the time of trial. Look at the examples given (Qur'an, supplication, idols) to understand how these modes work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الناس من عارضهم عند ظنهم وقوع التشابه بالعلم والوجود والكون وغير ذلك، وذلك لازم لو كان ثمة عقل يحتمل الإدراك، ولكنهم قوم أنكروا علم الضروريات وما هو في حد العيان، فلا معنى لمناظرتهم، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ونفى عنهم التدبير فيها، وأزال عنهم خلقها، وصير مشيئتهم فيها كبعض ما تتمنى به الأنفس أن يكون حقائق الأشياء خارجة منها، واحتجوا في ذلك بالأمر والنهي ثم الوعد والوعيد، ومحال مثله إلى ما للأمر والناهي حقيقته أو عليه وعنده وله / وعده على ما ذكرنا وتلوا ذلك آيات الأمر والنهي وذكر العقل ثم آيات الجزاء وهي بينه بحمد الله لمن قرأ القرآن. ثم هو قد سوعد على ذلك بما بينا في فساد قول المجبرة، وقالوا في الإضافة إلى الله: إنها تخرج على وجهين سوى حقيقة الفعل: أحدهما بالسبب الأفعال الأمر بالخيرات والتخلية في الشرور، وقد تضاف مع رجوع قدرة الذي كان منهم الأفعال إلى من له الأسباب وإن لم يكن حقيقتها له، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والثاني أن الإضافة إليه عند المحنة بما له بها حال التصديق والتكذيب كما أضيف إلى القرآن زادهم إيمانا ورجسا، وإلى الدعاء أنه زادهم نفورا، وإلى القوم أن أنسوهم ذكر الله وإلى الأصنام أن أهلكن كثيرا من الناس بما عبدوا، كانت أفعال.
And among the people are those who opposed them (the Jabriyya) when they thought there was similarity in knowledge, existence, and being, and other than that, and that is necessary if there were an intellect capable of perception, but they are a people who denied necessary knowledge and what is in the realm of sight, so there is no meaning in debating them, and there is no power except by Allah. And among them are those who affirmed actions for creation and negated from them management in them, and removed from them their creation, and made their will in them like some of what the souls wish for that the realities of things would be outside them, and they argued in that by command and prohibition and then promise and threat, and impossible is its like to what for the commander and prohibitor is its reality or upon him or with him or for him / his promise as we mentioned, and they recited verses of command and prohibition and mention of intellect, then verses of recompense, and they are clear, praise be to God, for whoever reads the Qur'an. Then he (the proponent) was aided in that by what we stated concerning the corruption of the saying of the Jabriyya. And they said concerning attribution to God: that it comes in two aspects besides real action: one of them by cause – the actions command of good and leaving of evil, and it may be attributed with the return of the power of the one who was from them of actions to the one who has the causes even if its reality is not for him, and there is no power except by Allah. And the second: that attribution to Him at the time of trial according to what He has of state of confirmation and denial, as was attributed to the Qur'an that it increased them in faith and abomination, and to the supplication that it increased them in aversion, and to the people that they forgot the remembrance of God, and to the idols that they destroyed many of the people because they worshipped, were actions.
Source pages p. 826

Commentary
This passage discusses two erroneous groups that emerged in response to the Jabriyya doctrine, followed by a nuanced position on attributing actions to God.

First group: Those who opposed the Jabriyya by claiming similarity (tashābuh) between God and creation in terms of knowledge, existence, etc. Maturidi dismisses them because they deny necessary knowledge and self-evident truths, making debate futile.

Second group: Those who affirmed that actions are truly performed by humans (taḥqīq al-afʿāl lil-khalq) but denied that humans have any management (tadbīr) or creation (khalq) of those actions. They reduced human will to mere wishes, like hoping something becomes real outside one's power. They relied on verses of command and prohibition and reward/punishment, and Maturidi notes that this position was aided by his own refutation of Jabriyya (perhaps indicating some overlap).

Then Maturidi reports that these thinkers proposed two ways of attributing actions to God besides real action:
1. **Attribution by cause (sabab)**: God commands good deeds and leaves evil deeds uncommanded; actions are attributed to God as the ultimate cause of the ability and the cause of the action, even if the action is not actually His.
2. **Attribution at the time of trial (miḥna)**: Attribution occurs according to the resulting state of faith or denial. Examples: The Qur'an is said to increase faith in believers and abomination in disbelievers; supplication increases aversion; people cause forgetfulness; idols cause destruction – these are attributions based on causal connection or occasion, not direct creation.

Maturidi presents these views as part of the discourse, without explicitly endorsing them, but he earlier indicated that the second group is mistaken (since they denied creation and management). The passage is descriptive of these opinions within the broader debate on human action and divine omnipotence.

Key Terms
التشابه
علم الضروريات
التحقيق
التدبير
الخلق
المشيئة
السبب
المحنة
التصديق
التكذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the second group's two modes of attribution fully resolve the problem of divine action, but Maturidi notes they still negated God's role in creation and management, which is problematic.
Correction: Attribution by cause or at trial does not affirm God's direct creation of actions; it only provides indirect connection, leaving God's creative power unacknowledged.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second way of attributing actions to God (besides real action) proposed by the group that affirmed human acts but negated creation?
A) Attribution by command and prohibition only.
B) Attribution by cause (sabab) where God commands good and leaves evil.
C) Attribution at the time of trial (miḥna) based on resulting faith or denial.
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that both denying necessary knowledge and denying God's management in actions are errors, and that attributing actions to God by cause or at trial does not fully resolve the problem without affirming divine creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a clear truth about God simply because it made you uncomfortable—like the reality that every single one of your actions is created and managed by Him? What does that rejection say about your trust in His sovereignty?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you genuinely feel that God created that action in you, or do you subtly credit yourself and merely acknowledge Him as a distant cause? How would your humility change if you believed He directly brought that action into existence?
?
Think of a time you attributed your failure or sin to 'the way God made me' or 'my circumstances' while denying your own responsibility. Which group's error does that resemble—the first or the second? What would it cost you to fully affirm both God's creation and your accountability?

Refutation of Those Who Affirm Actions but Deny Creation
Maturidi critiques those who ascribe actions to creatures but deny them creation and governance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of a group that affirms human actions but denies their creation and governance, and the flaw in their argument according to Maturidi.

Core Idea
Affirming actions without creation leads to incoherence.

Imam Maturidi identifies a group that attempts a middle ground: they affirm that humans perform actions but deny that humans create or govern those actions. Instead, they reduce human will to mere wishful thinking. Their proof relies on divine commands and threats, but Maturidi finds this argument impossible, as it fails to properly attribute the reality of command and prohibition. This lesson explores their position and Maturidi's critique.

Guided Path
1
Understand the group's position
The passage describes a group that affirms actions for creatures but denies them governance and creation, making their will like wishful thinking.
This is not the Jabriyya, who deny free will entirely.
2
Identify their proof
Their proof uses divine command, prohibition, promise, and threat. They also cite Quranic verses and intellect.
This proof is common among those who want to preserve human accountability without attributing creation to humans.
3
Grasp Maturidi's criticism
Maturidi says their argument is impossible because it fails to properly attribute the reality of command and prohibition. He points to the Quran as clear on this matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ونفى عنهم التدبير فيها ، وأزال عنهم خلقها ، وصير مشيئتهم فيها كبعض ما تتمنى به الأنفس أن يكون حقائق الأشياء خارجة منها ، واحتجوا فى ذلك بالأمر والنهي ثم الوعد والوعيد ، و محال مثله إلى ما للأمر والناهي حقيقته أو عليه وعنده وله / وعده على ما ذكرنا وتلوا ذلك آيات الأمر والنهى وذكر العقل ثم آيات الجزاء وهى بينه بحمد الله لمن قرأ القرآن .
And among them are those who affirmed the actions for the creatures but denied them governance in them, and removed from them their creation, and made their will in them like some of what the souls wish for that the realities of things come out from them. And they argued in that by command and prohibition, then promise and threat. And its like is impossible to what the commander and prohibiter have in terms of reality or upon him and with him and his promise as we mentioned. And they recited the verses of command and prohibition and mentioned the intellect, then verses of recompense, and they are clear, praise be to God, for whoever reads the Quran.
Source pages p. 826

Commentary
This passage introduces a group that affirms actions for creatures (they do actions) but denies that creatures have any governance (tadbīr) or creation of those actions. They reduce human will to mere wishful thinking. Their proof relies on divine commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. Maturidi finds this argument impossible because it fails to properly attribute the reality of command and prohibition. They also cite Quranic verses and reason, but Maturidi implies that the correct understanding is clear to those who read the Quran properly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans can be held accountable for actions they do not create or govern.
Correction: Maturidi argues that this position is impossible because it fails to properly attribute the reality of command and prohibition; true accountability requires some form of effective agency.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof used by the group mentioned in this passage?
A) Sensory experience
B) Divine command and prohibition, promise and threat
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Analogy with nature

Key Takeaway
Affirming human actions without granting them creation or governance leads to an incoherent notion of moral responsibility that cannot be supported by divine commands.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse like 'Allah commands you to be just,' do you truly believe that you have the real capacity to fulfill that command, or do you treat it as a mere wish like 'I hope I can be just'? How does your answer reveal your true belief about your own agency?
?
The group in this lesson made human will like a wish — something that longs for reality but never brings it about. Where in your life have you turned obedience to Allah into mere wishing, avoiding the decisive action that real faith requires?
?
If Allah's promises and threats are real, then your choices must be real too. Are you living today as if your next action carries eternal weight — or as if it is just a shadow without consequence? What will you change in the next hour to act as if your deeds truly matter?

Human Acquisition and Divine Creation Reconciled
Maturidi explains the reconciliation using opposite pairs and the concepts of kasb and khalq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi reconciles human accountability with divine creation through the concepts of kasb and khalq, using opposite pairs to show that an act is real from both aspects.

Core Idea
The act is human by acquisition and divine by creation—both are real, differing in aspect.

Maturidi addresses a central theological puzzle: if God creates everything, how can humans be responsible for their actions? He introduces the terms kasb (acquisition) and khalq (creation) to show that an action has two aspects: the servant acquires it, God creates it. This lesson unpacks his argument using opposite pairs and explains how this avoids the extremes of Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify key terms
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Locate the terms kasb (كسب) and khalq (خلق) and notice how they are used.
2
Analyze the opposite pairs
The passage lists pairs like misguidance/guidance, expansion/constriction. Notice that each pair is attributed to both God and humans, but in different respects (jiha).
These pairs illustrate that both attributions are real but from different directions.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the act is truly the servant's by kasb and truly God's by khalq. This avoids both compulsion and independent human creation.
This reconciliation is the heart of Maturidi's theology of action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ، وبها صاروا عصاة تقاه ، وجعلوها لله خلقا اعتبارا بما سبق من الإضافة إلى الله جل ثناؤه مرة وإلى العباد ثانيا ، والمذكور المضاف إلى العباد هو المضاف / إلى الله تعالى لا غير ، بمعنى يؤدى إلى اختلاف الجهة في العقل نحو الإضلال والإزاغة ، والهداية والعصمة ، ثم الإنعام والامتنان ، ثم الخذلان والمد ثم الزيادة من الوجهين ، ثم الطبع والتيسير ، ثم التشرح والتضييق ، هذه الأحوال ، على وجود مضادات ما يوصف بها ، وإضافة الاهتداء والضلالة ، والرشد والغى ، والاستقامة والزيغ إلى الخلق ، وكان في الوجهين تحقيق الآخر ، إذ لا يضاف الذى أضيف إلى الله مطلقا ، أضداد الواقع عليه معانيها ، ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك الفعل الذي هو للعباد من طريق الكسب ، [و]الله من طريق الخلق ؛ دليل ذلك أن فعل الله تعالى في التحقيق خلقه ، وكل ذلك لو أضيف إليه باسم الخلق لم يفهم منه في ذلك غير إنشاء ، وفهم من الذى منهم من العبد فعله وكسبه نحو أن نقول : خلق الشرح والضيق ، وخلق الضلال والاهتداء ونحو ذلك ، فمثله الأول . مع ما لو جاز صرف أحد الوجهين عن حقيقة المفهوم أو الأسباب أو الأحوال فالآخر مثله ، وكل ذلك .. مجاز لا حقيقة ؛ ولذلك جاء مقابلة القولين [من] الجبرية والقدرية ، وهذا معنى
And among them are those who affirmed the actions for the creatures, and by them they became disobedient to piety, and made them for God as creation, considering the previous attribution to God the Exalted once and to the servants a second time. And what is mentioned as attributed to the servants is what is attributed to God Most High, no difference, in a manner that leads to difference of direction (jiha) in the intellect, such as misguidance and deviation, guidance and protection, then bestowal and gratitude, then abandonment and extension, then increase from both sides, then sealing and facilitation, then expansion and constriction. These states, upon the existence of their opposites by which they are described, and the attribution of guidance and misguidance, right direction and error, uprightness and deviation to the creatures, and in the two directions is the realization of the other. For what is attributed to God is not attributed absolutely; it is the opposites that occur upon their meanings. It is established that the reality of that act which belongs to the servants is by way of acquisition (kasb), and to God by way of creation (khalq). The proof of that is that the act of God Most High in reality is His creation. And all of that, if attributed to Him by the name of creation, nothing is understood from that except origination. And what is understood from what is from them of the servant is his act and his acquisition, like when we say: He created expansion and constriction, and He created misguidance and guidance, and so on. So the first is like that. And with that, if it were permissible to turn aside one of the two directions from the reality of the concept or the causes or the states, the other is like that. And all that is metaphor (majāz), not reality. Therefore the two statements (of Jabriyya and Qadariyya) are contrasted, and this is the meaning.
Source pages p. 827

Commentary
This passage presents the reconciliation of human free will and divine creation through the concepts of acquisition (kasb) and creation (khalq). A group affirms actions for creatures (they are doers) but makes them creations of God, drawing on earlier bidirectional attribution: once to God, once to servants. The attribution to servants is the same as to God but differs in direction (jiha) in the intellect. Examples of opposite pairs (misguidance/guidance, etc.) show that both God and creatures are attributed with these, but in different respects. The reality is that the act belongs to the servant by way of acquisition (kasb) and to God by way of creation (khalq). Proof: God's act is creation (invention), while the servant's act is his own deed and acquisition. Using the phrase 'He created expansion and constriction' does not imply God does the actual expanding/constricting; it is a metaphorical attribution. Similarly, all such attributions are metaphorical (majāz), not literal. Thus the two extreme positions (Jabriyya and Qadariyya) are both avoided.

Key Terms
كسب (acquisition)
خلق (creation)
جهة (direction/aspect)
مجاز (metaphor)
حقيقة (reality)
إضلال (misguidance)
هداية (guidance)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think kasb means humans partially create their actions, while Maturidi holds that humans acquire actions that are entirely created by God.
Correction: Kasb means the servant is genuinely the agent of the act, but the act is created by God. This avoids both compulsion and full self-determination.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the relationship between human action and divine creation?
A) Humans create their own actions independently.
B) God creates the action and humans acquire (kasb) it.
C) God does everything and humans have no role.
D) Actions are purely metaphorical with no reality.

Key Takeaway
The act is truly the servant's by acquisition and truly God's by creation—both are real, differing only in aspect, avoiding the extremes of Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own obedience and disobedience, do you truly feel both that you are responsible and that God creates and governs the act? Which aspect do you tend to emphasize, and what does that reveal about your heart?
?
Think of a specific sin you committed. How does acknowledging both your acquisition of that sin and God's creation of it change the way you approach repentance and reliance on Him for guidance?
?
Maturidi says both attributions are real, not metaphor. Are you willing to accept that your actions are truly yours and truly from God? Does this make you more grateful for guidance and more fearful of misguidance, and what step will you take today to act on that?

The Metaphorical Nature of Attributions to God
Maturidi uses similes to explain metaphorical attribution to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses metaphorical examples to explain that attributions to God are not always literal.

Core Idea
Attributions to God often carry conditions and are not literal.

Maturidi begins by showing that the way we attribute things to God is similar to how we attribute deception to the worldly life or speech to ruins—metaphorically. This sets the stage for understanding divine actions without falling into anthropomorphism or literalism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the similes Maturidi uses.
2
Identify the three examples
The passage gives three examples of metaphorical attribution: the world of deception, deserted villages, and animals. Find each one and note what is being attributed and why it is metaphorical.
All three share the feature that the thing attributed is not literally done by the subject.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself why Maturidi starts with these examples. How does this prepare for the discussion of divine actions?
This connects to the core idea that attributions to God are not to be taken in a crude literal sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البشر أولئك ، فمثله الإضافة إلى الله. وقد يحتمل الأحوال كما أضيف إلى الدنيا الغرور وإلى زينتها بما هي تظهر ما يكون مثله الغرور ، وإن لم يكن منها حق الفعل، وكذا ما أضيف إلى القرى الخاوية على عروشها والقيود من النطق، وإلى البهائم من الشكاية مما لو كانت تنطق بقول ، فمثله في الإضافة إلى الله . بما منه من الإمهال وإظهار النعم الذى كاد أن يكون حجة لهم في الرضا بأفعالهم ؛ ولذلك ظنوا أن الله أمرهم بما هم فيه من الأفعال بالإمهال والتأخير ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ، وبها صاروا عصاة تقاه ، وجعلوها لله خلقا اعتبارا بما سبق من الإضافة إلى الله جل ثناؤه مرة وإلى العباد ثانيا ، والمذكور المضاف إلى العباد هو المضاف إلى الله تعالى لا غير ، بمعنى يؤدى إلى اختلاف الجهة في العقل نحو الإضلال والإزاغة ، والهداية والعصمة ، ثم الإنعام والامتنان ، ثم الخذلان والمد ثم الزيادة من الوجهين ، ثم الطبع والتيسير ، ثم التشرح والتضييق ، هذه الأحوال ، على وجود مضادات ما يوصف بها ، وإضافة الاهتداء والضلالة ، والرشد والغى ، والاستقامة والزيغ إلى الخلق ، وكان في الوجهين تحقيق الآخر ، إذ لا يضاف الذى أضيف إلى الله مطلقا ، أضداد الواقع عليه معانيها ، ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك الفعل الذي هو للعباد من طريق الكسب ، والله من طريق الخلق ؛ دليل ذلك أن فعل الله تعالى في التحقيق خلقه ، وكل ذلك لو أضيف إليه باسم الخلق لم يفهم منه في ذلك غير إنشاء ، وفهم من الذى منهم من العبد فعله وكسبه نحو أن نقول : خلق الشرح والضيق ، وخلق الضلال والاهتداء ونحو ذلك ، فمثله الأول . مع ما لو جاز صرف أحد الوجهين عن حقيقة المفهوم أو الأسباب أو الأحوال فالآخر مثله ، وكل ذلك مجاز لا حقيقة ؛ ولذلك جاء مقابلة القولين من الجبرية والقدرية ، وهذا معنى ما روى من لعن المرجئة والقدرية . إن المرجئة أرجأت الأفعال إلى الله ولم تجعلها للعبد ، والقدرية أثبتتها لله على ما تنسب الخلق إلى الله تعالى ، ولم تجعل الله فيها تدبيرا . والعدل هو القول بتحقيق الأمرين ؛ ليكون الله موصوفا بما وصف به نفسه محمودا به كما قال : خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وقال : فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قدير ، وليكون عدلا مفصلا كما قال : وَمَا رَبُّكَ لظَلَّامٍ لِلعَبِيدِ ، وقال : وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ لاتَّبَعْتُم الشَّيْطَانَ إِلَّا قَلِيلا
Those people, so similarly is the attribution to God. And it may carry conditions just as attribution is made to the world of deception and to its adornment in that it shows what is like deception, even if there is no real act from it, and likewise what is attributed to the deserted villages and to the restrictions of speech, and to the animals of complaint as if they could speak words, so similarly is the attribution to God. Because of the respite and display of blessings which almost became an argument for them in being pleased with their deeds; therefore they thought that God commanded them regarding what they are doing of deeds by respite and delay, and there is no power except with God. And among them are those who verified deeds for creation, and by it they became disobedient to piety, and they made them for God as creation considering the previous attribution to God Almighty once and to servants a second time. The mentioned attribution to servants is the same attribution to God Almighty, not otherwise, in a sense that leads to a difference of aspect in reason such as misguidance and causing to stray, guidance and protection, then bestowal and obligation, then abandonment and extension, then increase from both aspects, then sealing and facilitation, then expansion and constriction — these conditions, upon the existence of opposites of what they are described with, and attribution of guidance and misguidance, right direction and error, uprightness and deviation to creation, and in both aspects the verification of the other, since what is attributed to God absolutely is not added to opposites of what its meanings occur upon, it is established that the reality of that act which belongs to servants is by way of acquisition, and to God by way of creation. Evidence of that is that the act of God Almighty in reality is His creation, and all of that if attributed to Him by the name of creation nothing else is understood from it except origination, and it is understood from what is from them of the servant's act and his acquisition, such as we say: He created expansion and constriction, and created misguidance and guidance and so on, so the first is similar. And if it were permissible to turn one of the two aspects from the reality of the understood or the causes or conditions, then the other would be like it, and all that is metaphor, not reality; therefore the opposing of the two sayings of the Jabriyya and Qadariyya came. And this is the meaning of what was narrated about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. Indeed the Murji'a deferred actions to God and did not make them for the servant, and the Qadariyya affirmed them for God in the way they attribute creation to God Almighty, and did not make God have any disposal in them. And justice is the statement of verifying both matters; so that God may be described with what He described Himself with, praised by it, as He said: 'Creator of everything' and said: 'He is over everything powerful,' and so that He may be perfectly just as He said: 'And your Lord is not unjust to the servants,' and said: 'And if not for the favor of God upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Satan except a few.'
Source pages p. 827

Commentary
This passage defines the correct attribution of actions to God and humans, contrasting it with the extreme views of the Jabriyya (Murji'a) and Qadariyya. Maturidi begins by explaining that attributions to God are often metaphorical, like ascribing 'deception' to the worldly life even though it is not a real agent. He then discusses those who attribute all actions fully to creation (the Qadariyya), saying they became disobedient by that, and those who attribute them solely to God (the Jabriyya/Murji'a) while neglecting human responsibility. He introduces key terms such as 'kash' (acquisition) for humans and 'khalq' (creation) for God. The proof for this dual attribution is that when an act is attributed to God as creation, it means origination ex nihilo; when attributed to a servant, it means his own act and acquisition. The two aspects are not contradictory but complementary. Maturidi then cites the condemnation of both extremes in tradition: the Murji'a defer all actions to God without human part, and the Qadariyya affirm actions for God only nominally without God's effective disposal. The just view ('adl) is to affirm both aspects, as God is described in the Quran as Creator of everything and Powerful over all, yet not unjust to servants, and His grace is necessary for guidance. This balanced position avoids the extremes of determinism and absolute free will.

Key Terms
الإضافة
الغرور
الدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think that if God is attributed with an action, He does it literally in a human sense.
Correction: Maturidi shows that attribution is often metaphorical, carrying conditions; divine actions must be understood appropriately.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the examples of 'world of deception', 'deserted villages', and 'animals'?
A) God directly performs all actions.
B) Attributions can be metaphorical and not imply literal agency.
C) Humans are the true agents behind all actions.
D) Animals can actually speak.

Key Takeaway
Attributions to God are not always literal; they can carry conditions, as illustrated by everyday metaphorical language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an action you have done that you justify by saying 'God gave me the ability' or 'God delayed punishment.' How does Maturidi's teaching about the condition of respite challenge your assumption that God approves of that action? Will you examine your deeds differently now?
?
You often attribute your successes to God's blessings. But do you ever use those blessings as an excuse to continue in sin? How can you ensure that your attribution of blessings to God is not a cover for complacency?
?
Maturidi uses the analogy of metaphorical attribution to show that God's role is not always literal. How does this affect the way you view your own responsibility for your actions? Are you ready to take full accountability without hiding behind divine decree?

The Two Extremes: Jabriyya and Qadariyya
Maturidi critiques the two extreme sects and introduces dual attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the errors of the Jabriyya (Murji'a) and Qadariyya regarding the attribution of actions.

Core Idea
Both extremes err: one denies human responsibility, the other denies divine disposal.

After establishing the metaphorical nature of attribution, Maturidi critiques two opposing sects. The Jabriyya attribute all actions to God alone, while the Qadariyya attribute them fully to humans. Both miss the balanced view of divine creation and human acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the description of each sect.
Pay attention to the hadith mentioned.
2
Identify the two sects and their errors
The passage first mentions a group that 'verified deeds for creation' (Qadariyya) and then those who 'deferred actions to God' (Murji'a/Jabriyya). List their key characteristics and why they are wrong.
The hadith about cursing both groups emphasizes their deviation.
3
Understand the dual attribution
Maturidi explains that the same actions are attributed to both God and servants but in different aspects. Notice the list of opposites (guidance/misguidance, etc.) and how they are attributed.
This is a crucial nuance.
4
Reflect on the dangers of each extreme
Consider how each extreme undermines either divine justice or human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you find yourself making excuses (like 'it was my fate') or feeling utterly helpless? How does this lesson's teaching on dual attribution compel you to take full ownership of your actions while still relying on God's mercy?
?
Do you ever secretly resent God for your life's difficulties, as if He alone is responsible without your own choices playing a role? How would accepting that God creates the situation but you acquire your response change your attitude?
?
This lesson warns that taking either extreme (all to God or all to you) is a distortion. Have you ever comforted yourself by denying your own fault in a sin, blaming it all on God? What would it look like to sincerely repent while acknowledging that God created the action and you acquired it?

The Just View: Divine Creation and Human Acquisition
Maturidi concludes with the just view of 'adl and Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the balanced position of 'adl: actions are from God by creation and from humans by acquisition, supported by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Justice lies in affirming both divine creation and human acquisition.

Maturidi concludes by presenting the correct view: actions are created by God but acquired by humans. He supports this with Quranic verses showing God as Creator and Just, and that humans need His grace. This avoids the pitfalls of both extremes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the definition of 'adl and the Quranic proofs.
Notice the two Quranic passages cited.
2
Identify the two aspects of 'adl
Maturidi says 'adl is 'verifying both matters'. Find what those two matters are and how they relate to God's attributes.
One aspect is God's power and creation, the other is His justice and grace.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
List the Quranic verses and explain how each supports the balanced view: 'Creator of everything' shows creation, 'not unjust' shows justice, 'if not for God's favor' shows need for grace.
These verses together uphold both divine sovereignty and human accountability.
4
Reflect on the middle path
Consider how 'adl avoids the errors of Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البشر أولئك ، فمثله الإضافة إلى الله. وقد يحتمل الأحوال كما أضيف إلى الدنيا الغرور وإلى زينتها بما هي تظهر ما يكون مثله الغرور ، وإن لم يكن منها حق الفعل، وكذا ما أضيف إلى القرى الخاوية على عروشها والقيود من النطق، وإلى البهائم من الشكاية مما لو كانت تنطق بقول ، فمثله في الإضافة إلى الله . بما منه من الإمهال وإظهار النعم الذى كاد أن يكون حجة لهم في الرضا بأفعالهم ؛ ولذلك ظنوا أن الله أمرهم بما هم فيه من الأفعال بالإمهال والتأخير ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ومنهم من حقق الأفعال للخلق ، وبها صاروا عصاة تقاه ، وجعلوها لله خلقا اعتبارا بما سبق من الإضافة إلى الله جل ثناؤه مرة وإلى العباد ثانيا ، والمذكور المضاف إلى العباد هو المضاف إلى الله تعالى لا غير ، بمعنى يؤدى إلى اختلاف الجهة في العقل نحو الإضلال والإزاغة ، والهداية والعصمة ، ثم الإنعام والامتنان ، ثم الخذلان والمد ثم الزيادة من الوجهين ، ثم الطبع والتيسير ، ثم التشرح والتضييق ، هذه الأحوال ، على وجود مضادات ما يوصف بها ، وإضافة الاهتداء والضلالة ، والرشد والغى ، والاستقامة والزيغ إلى الخلق ، وكان في الوجهين تحقيق الآخر ، إذ لا يضاف الذى أضيف إلى الله مطلقا ، أضداد الواقع عليه معانيها ، ثبت أن حقيقة ذلك الفعل الذي هو للعباد من طريق الكسب ، والله من طريق الخلق ؛ دليل ذلك أن فعل الله تعالى في التحقيق خلقه ، وكل ذلك لو أضيف إليه باسم الخلق لم يفهم منه في ذلك غير إنشاء ، وفهم من الذى منهم من العبد فعله وكسبه نحو أن نقول : خلق الشرح والضيق ، وخلق الضلال والاهتداء ونحو ذلك ، فمثله الأول . مع ما لو جاز صرف أحد الوجهين عن حقيقة المفهوم أو الأسباب أو الأحوال فالآخر مثله ، وكل ذلك مجاز لا حقيقة ؛ ولذلك جاء مقابلة القولين من الجبرية والقدرية ، وهذا معنى ما روى من لعن المرجئة والقدرية . إن المرجئة أرجأت الأفعال إلى الله ولم تجعلها للعبد ، والقدرية أثبتتها لله على ما تنسب الخلق إلى الله تعالى ، ولم تجعل الله فيها تدبيرا . والعدل هو القول بتحقيق الأمرين ؛ ليكون الله موصوفا بما وصف به نفسه محمودا به كما قال : خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ وقال : فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قدير ، وليكون عدلا مفصلا كما قال : وَمَا رَبُّكَ لظَلَّامٍ لِلعَبِيدِ ، وقال : وَلَوْلَا فَضْلُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَتُهُ لاتَّبَعْتُم الشَّيْطَانَ إِلَّا قَلِيلا
Those people, so similarly is the attribution to God. And it may carry conditions just as attribution is made to the world of deception and to its adornment in that it shows what is like deception, even if there is no real act from it, and likewise what is attributed to the deserted villages and to the restrictions of speech, and to the animals of complaint as if they could speak words, so similarly is the attribution to God. Because of the respite and display of blessings which almost became an argument for them in being pleased with their deeds; therefore they thought that God commanded them regarding what they are doing of deeds by respite and delay, and there is no power except with God. And among them are those who verified deeds for creation, and by it they became disobedient to piety, and they made them for God as creation considering the previous attribution to God Almighty once and to servants a second time. The mentioned attribution to servants is the same attribution to God Almighty, not otherwise, in a sense that leads to a difference of aspect in reason such as misguidance and causing to stray, guidance and protection, then bestowal and obligation, then abandonment and extension, then increase from both aspects, then sealing and facilitation, then expansion and constriction — these conditions, upon the existence of opposites of what they are described with, and attribution of guidance and misguidance, right direction and error, uprightness and deviation to creation, and in both aspects the verification of the other, since what is attributed to God absolutely is not added to opposites of what its meanings occur upon, it is established that the reality of that act which belongs to servants is by way of acquisition, and to God by way of creation. Evidence of that is that the act of God Almighty in reality is His creation, and all of that if attributed to Him by the name of creation nothing else is understood from it except origination, and it is understood from what is from them of the servant's act and his acquisition, such as we say: He created expansion and constriction, and created misguidance and guidance and so on, so the first is similar. And if it were permissible to turn one of the two aspects from the reality of the understood or the causes or conditions, then the other would be like it, and all that is metaphor, not reality; therefore the opposing of the two sayings of the Jabriyya and Qadariyya came. And this is the meaning of what was narrated about cursing the Murji'a and Qadariyya. Indeed the Murji'a deferred actions to God and did not make them for the servant, and the Qadariyya affirmed them for God in the way they attribute creation to God Almighty, and did not make God have any disposal in them. And justice is the statement of verifying both matters; so that God may be described with what He described Himself with, praised by it, as He said: 'Creator of everything' and said: 'He is over everything powerful,' and so that He may be perfectly just as He said: 'And your Lord is not unjust to the servants,' and said: 'And if not for the favor of God upon you and His mercy, you would have followed Satan except a few.'
Source pages p. 827

Commentary
This passage defines the correct attribution of actions to God and humans, contrasting it with the extreme views of the Jabriyya (Murji'a) and Qadariyya. Maturidi begins by explaining that attributions to God are often metaphorical, like ascribing 'deception' to the worldly life even though it is not a real agent. He then discusses those who attribute all actions fully to creation (the Qadariyya), saying they became disobedient by that, and those who attribute them solely to God (the Jabriyya/Murji'a) while neglecting human responsibility. He introduces key terms such as 'kash' (acquisition) for humans and 'khalq' (creation) for God. The proof for this dual attribution is that when an act is attributed to God as creation, it means origination ex nihilo; when attributed to a servant, it means his own act and acquisition. The two aspects are not contradictory but complementary. Maturidi then cites the condemnation of both extremes in tradition: the Murji'a defer all actions to God without human part, and the Qadariyya affirm actions for God only nominally without God's effective disposal. The just view ('adl) is to affirm both aspects, as God is described in the Quran as Creator of everything and Powerful over all, yet not unjust to servants, and His grace is necessary for guidance. This balanced position avoids the extremes of determinism and absolute free will.

Key Takeaway
The just view ('adl) is that God creates actions and humans acquire them, as supported by Quranic verses on creation, power, justice, and grace.
