Refuting Objections on Divine Creation and Human Choice
Maturidi refutes an objection against divine creation of actions by reaffirming human choice and moral accountability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the objection that God's creation of actions negates human responsibility, by affirming that the servant's act is real and chosen, and that God's creation does not imply compulsion.

Core Idea
Divine creation of actions does not compel—the servant still chooses, making moral accountability meaningful.

Maturidi continues his defense of the Ash'ari position on qadar by addressing a further objection: if God creates all actions, then why call anyone else 'creator'? He responds by returning to the established principle that the servant has a real act and choice. In this passage, he clarifies that God's knowledge, predestination, and naming of the act do not negate human agency—rather, they make command, prohibition, punishment, and reward consistent. He warns that those who deny this are following an illusion born of ignorance of divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the objection-and-response structure.
2
Identify the key principle
Maturidi states that the servant has a real act and that he chooses it. This is the foundation for rebutting the objection.
The term 'حقيقة' (reality) is crucial.
3
Understand the non-compulsion argument
God's creation of the act does not push, compel, or coerce the servant. This is essential for preserving moral responsibility.
Look for the words 'لم يدفعه', 'لم يحمله', 'لم يضطره'.
4
Connect to moral accountability
Because there is no compulsion, command, prohibition, punishment, and reward are meaningful. Reflect on how this counters the objection.
Maturidi lists divine actions that coexist with human choice.
5
Consider the concluding warning
Maturidi warns that denying God's creation based on such objections is ignorance of wisdom. The passage ends with a call to submission.
The final phrases may be ambiguous but emphasize reliance on God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يعارض تسمية غير الذى خلق الموت وأحوال الخلق أحق من الذي خلق ، وهو بالجملة مُسمّى أنه خالق ذلك ، فمهما قال في ذلك فهو جواب له فى الأول : والأصل أنه ثبت للعبد فعل فى الحقيقة ، وأنه له يختار ، وأنه آثر الأشياء عنده وأحبها ، وأن خلق ذلك لم يدفعه إليه ، ولم يحمله ولم يضطره إليه ، فوجود ذلك ووجود علمه به وخبره عنه وإثباته فى اللوح المحفوظ وايجاب معاداته لوقت فعله و تسميته بما سمى ، إذ لم يضطره إلى فعله ولا حمله عليه ، حسن معه الأمر والنهى والتعذيب والإثابة . ومن أنكر بهذا خلقه فتعلقه بهذا النوع خيال ، وحقه أن ينظر الوجه الذى به يعرف خلق الأشياء ، فإن أمكن تحقيقه فالإنكار بهذا النوع إنما هو جهل بالحكمة . وعلى ذلك كان أول ما جبل عليه فيعلم إن خضع للمكرم به إن شاء الله ، وإن لم يمكن تسقط المسألة ، ويفضل الذي عارض کله ، ولا قوة إلا بالله به
Then he counters the naming of other than the one who created death and the states of creation as more deserving than the one who created, and it is in summary that He is named Creator of that, so whatever he says in that, it is a response to him in the first: And the principle is that a real act is established for the servant, and that he chooses it, and that he prefers things according to him and loves them, and that the creation of that did not push it to him, nor compel him, nor coerce him to it. So the existence of that, and the existence of His knowledge of it, and His report of it, and its inscription in the Preserved Tablet, and the necessity of His enmity at the time of his act, and his naming it by what it is named, since He did not coerce him to his act nor compel him to it, makes good with it both command and prohibition, punishment and reward. Whoever denies His creation by this, his attachment to this type is illusion, and his right is to look at the aspect by which the creation of things is known, for if its verification is possible, then denial in this manner is only ignorance of wisdom. And upon that was the first thing he was created for, so he knows if he submits to the honored one if Allah wills, and if it is not possible, the question drops, and the one who objects is refuted entirely, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 842

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection that someone other than God (like an idol) might be more deserving of being called 'creator' of death and states of creation. Maturidi responds by reaffirming the principle: the servant has a real act and choice—he prefers and loves certain things. God's creation of the act does not push, compel, or coerce the servant into acting. Because God does not coerce, His knowledge, predestination, and naming of the act do not negate human responsibility; rather, they make command, prohibition, punishment, and reward meaningful. Those who deny God's creation based on this type of objection are clinging to an illusion. If one properly considers the aspect by which things are created, he will see that denial is due to ignorance of divine wisdom. The passage ends by noting that the first thing a person is created for is to submit to the honored (perhaps God or the Prophet), and if that is not realized, the question falls away and the objector is refuted.

Key Terms
اضطرار (compulsion)
اختيار (choice)
أمر ونهى (command and prohibition)
حكمة (wisdom)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates all actions, then humans are compelled and have no real choice.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that divine creation does not compel; the servant's act is real and chosen, which makes commands and punishments just.

Checkpoint
What makes command, prohibition, punishment, and reward valid according to Maturidi?
A) God creates the act without any human involvement.
B) The servant's act is real and chosen by him, not compelled by God.
C) Only good acts are created by God.
D) Humans create their own acts independently of God.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi defends human responsibility by distinguishing divine creation from compulsion, showing that God's predestination does not negate genuine choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent sin you committed. If God created that act, did He compel you? Or did you choose it? How does the distinction between creation and compulsion change the way you view your own guilt and your need to repent?
?
Do you sometimes blame your circumstances or even divine decree for your failures? What would it mean to fully accept that your choices are real and that God's creation of your acts does not lessen your accountability? How would that change your daily effort to obey?
?
If you truly believe that God's creation of your actions does not force you, then why do you still hesitate to obey when you know what is right? What fear or excuse is holding you back, and what does this lesson say about that excuse?

Actions as Divine Creation and Human Acquisition (Part 1)
Maturidi introduces the dual perspective of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dual aspect of human actions: as God's wise creation and as the servant's morally discerned act.

Core Idea
Every action is both God's creation and the servant's acquisition.

Maturidi opens his discussion on human actions by establishing that they have two aspects. When viewed as God's creation, they are true and wise; when viewed as the servant's act, they are subject to moral judgment. This distinction is essential for understanding divine justice and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note that the passage contrasts two perspectives: from God and from the servant.
2
Identify the dual aspect
The passage says the action from God's aspect is truth and wisdom, from the servant's aspect is foolishness and sin. Understand this distinction.
This is the foundational idea.
3
Analyze the example
Consider the example of reporting the disbeliever's act. Why is one report a lie and another truthful? Because the truth depends on the aspect from which the act is reported.
4
Relate to divine justice
Reflect on how this dual aspect helps reconcile God's creation of all actions with moral accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كان جاهلا ومن [؟] كتاب التوحيد [؟] مذموما ، وهو من هذا الوجه حق وحكمة ، والفعل من حيث العبد سفه وجور ، ذلك الوجه قبيح ومعصية . ألا ترى أن من عرف فعل الكافر على ما هو عنده أخبر به كان كاذبا ، ومن عرفه على ما عليه حقيقته كان عالما حكيما ، ولو أخبر به كان صادقا ، فعلى ذلك خلق الله ذلك وجعله على ما هو عليه ، وفعل العبد [لا] . وعلى قول من يجعل خلق الشيء غيره لا معنى له ؛ لأن فعل الله فى الحقيقة ليس بكفر ولا جور ولا سفه ، ولا الذي كان من العبد من خضوع وذلة وطاعة ومعصية ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يعارض تسمية غير الذي خلق الموت وأحوال الخلق أحق من الذي خلق ، وهو بالجملة مسمّى أنه خالق ذلك ، فمهما قال في ذلك فهو جواب له فى الأول : والأصل أنه ثبت للعبد فعل فى الحقيقة ، وأنه له يختار ، وأنه آثر الأشياء عنده وأحبها ، وأن خلق ذلك لم يدفعه إليه ، ولم يحمله ولم يضطره إليه ، فوجود ذلك ووجود علمه به وخبره عنه وإثباته فى اللوح المحفوظ وايجاب معاداته لوقت فعله و تسميته بما سمى ، إذ لم يضطره إلى فعله ولا حمله عليه ، حسن معه الأمر والنهى والتعذيب والإثابة . ومن أنكر بهذا خلقه فتعلقه بهذا النوع خيال ، وحقه أن ينظر الوجه الذى به يعرف خلق الأشياء ، فإن أمكن تحقيقه فالإنكار بهذا النوع إنما هو جهل بالحكمة . وعلى ذلك كان أول ما جبل عليه فيعلم إن خضع للمكرم به إن شاء الله ، وإن لم يمكن تسقط المسألة ، ويفضل الذي عارض كله ، ولا قوة إلا بالله به
And whoever was ignorant and from [?] the book of Tawhid [?] blameworthy, and it is from this aspect truth and wisdom, and the action from the perspective of the servant is foolishness and injustice, that aspect is ugly and disobedience. Do you not see that whoever knows the act of the disbeliever as it is in his view, if he informs of it, he is a liar, but whoever knows it as it is in its reality, he is knowing and wise, and if he informs of it, he is truthful. So similarly, God created that and made it as it is, and the act of the servant [is not?]. And according to the statement of whoever makes the creation of a thing other than it, it has no meaning; because the act of God in reality is not unbelief nor injustice nor foolishness, nor is that which came from the servant of humility and lowliness and obedience and disobedience, and there is no power except with God. Then he opposes the naming of other than the one who created death and the states of creation is more deserving than the one who created, and it is in summary named that He is the creator of that, so whatever he says in that, it is an answer to him in the first: and the principle is that it is established that the servant has an act in reality, and that he chooses for it, and that he prefers things in his view and loves them, and that the creation of that did not push him to it, nor compel him, nor constrain him to it, so the existence of that and the existence of His knowledge of it and His report about it and its affirmation in the Preserved Tablet and the requirement of His enmity for the time of his act and His naming it with what He named, since He did not constrain him to his act nor compel him to it, is consistent with command and prohibition and punishment and reward. And whoever denies this about His creation and clings to this type is an illusion, and his duty is to consider the aspect by which the creation of things is known, for if its verification is possible, then denial in this manner is ignorance of wisdom. And upon that was the first thing he was created with, so that he knows if he submits to the honored one by it if God wills, and if it is not possible, the question falls, and the one who opposes all of that is preferred, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 842

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing the two aspects of human actions: as divine creation and as human acquisition. Maturidi begins by stating that an action considered from the aspect of God's creation is true and wise, but from the aspect of the servant it may be foolishness and sin. He illustrates with the example of knowing the disbeliever's act: if one reports it as the disbeliever sees it, that report is false; but if one reports it as it really is (i.e., as God's creation), that report is true. Therefore, God's creation of the act is just, while the servant's act is subject to moral judgment. He then addresses those who deny that the servant has a real act, arguing that such a denial renders the distinction meaningless. Instead, it is established that the servant has a real act and chooses it, and that God's creation does not compel him. Hence, divine command, prohibition, punishment, and reward are consistent with this reality. Those who deny this and cling to objections are following an illusion and fail to understand the wisdom behind the divine decree. Maturidi concludes that this principle is the foundational disposition upon which humans are created.

Key Terms
فعل
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's creation of actions makes the servant not responsible for his acts.
Correction: Maturidi explains that actions have two aspects: God's wise creation and the servant's acquired act, so the servant is accountable.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the result when one reports the act of a disbeliever according to the disbeliever's own perspective?
A) He is truthful.
B) He is a liar.
C) He is wise.
D) He is ignorant.

Key Takeaway
Actions have two aspects: from God, they are wise and just; from the servant, they are subject to moral judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you tend to attribute the action entirely to your own choice or entirely to God's decree? How does Maturidi's dual perspective challenge you to hold both truths simultaneously, and what difference would that make in how you repent?
?
Think of a recent situation where you judged someone else's sin harshly. If you had first considered that action as God's creation (wise) before seeing it as the person's acquisition (sinful), would your reaction have changed? What one thing will you do this week to practice seeing the divine wisdom in actions you dislike?
?
You claim to believe that God creates all actions, yet you still feel guilt for your sins. Does this lesson make you more or less accountable for your deeds? Honestly, do you use divine decree as an excuse to avoid effort or repentance? What concrete step will you take today to own your actions before God?

Actions as Divine Creation and Human Acquisition (Part 2)
Maturidi refutes denial of the servant's real act and establishes human choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the servant has a real act and free choice, and that God's creation does not compel, making divine reward and punishment just.

Core Idea
The servant chooses his acts; God's creation does not compel.

In this passage, Maturidi refutes those who deny that the servant has a real act. He argues that such denial makes God's creation meaningless. Instead, it is established that the servant truly acts and chooses, and God's creation does not force him. This upholds the justice of divine commands and rewards.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the second part where Maturidi refutes those who deny the servant's real act.
2
Understand the refutation
Maturidi argues that denying the servant's act makes God's act meaningless. Because God's act in reality is not unbelief or injustice.
3
Grasp the principle
The passage states the principle: the servant has a real act, chooses it, and is not compelled by God's creation.
4
See the consistency
Note that because the servant is not compelled, divine commands, prohibitions, rewards, and punishments are consistent with justice.

Actions as Divine Creation and Human Acquisition (Part 3)
Maturidi concludes by rebuking deniers and stressing the need for proper understanding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that denying the servant's acquisition is an illusion rooted in ignorance of divine wisdom.

Core Idea
Denial of the servant's act is an illusion, not wisdom.

In the concluding part of his argument, Maturidi warns that those who deny the reality of human acquisition are following an illusion. He calls them to consider the aspect through which creation is truly known. This passage emphasizes the importance of correct understanding for theological coherence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the final part where Maturidi warns against denying this view.
2
Identify the illusion
The passage calls denial an illusion and says the denier should consider the aspect by which creation is known.
3
Understand the consequence
If verification is possible, denial is ignorance. If not, the question falls. This emphasizes the need for proper understanding.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with the idea that this is the foundational disposition of humans. This ties back to the beginning.

ومن كان جاهلا ومن [؟] كتاب التوحيد [؟] مذموما ، وهو من هذا الوجه حق وحكمة ، والفعل من حيث العبد سفه وجور ، ذلك الوجه قبيح ومعصية . ألا ترى أن من عرف فعل الكافر على ما هو عنده أخبر به كان كاذبا ، ومن عرفه على ما عليه حقيقته كان عالما حكيما ، ولو أخبر به كان صادقا ، فعلى ذلك خلق الله ذلك وجعله على ما هو عليه ، وفعل العبد [لا] . وعلى قول من يجعل خلق الشيء غيره لا معنى له ؛ لأن فعل الله فى الحقيقة ليس بكفر ولا جور ولا سفه ، ولا الذي كان من العبد من خضوع وذلة وطاعة ومعصية ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم يعارض تسمية غير الذي خلق الموت وأحوال الخلق أحق من الذي خلق ، وهو بالجملة مسمّى أنه خالق ذلك ، فمهما قال في ذلك فهو جواب له فى الأول : والأصل أنه ثبت للعبد فعل فى الحقيقة ، وأنه له يختار ، وأنه آثر الأشياء عنده وأحبها ، وأن خلق ذلك لم يدفعه إليه ، ولم يحمله ولم يضطره إليه ، فوجود ذلك ووجود علمه به وخبره عنه وإثباته فى اللوح المحفوظ وايجاب معاداته لوقت فعله و تسميته بما سمى ، إذ لم يضطره إلى فعله ولا حمله عليه ، حسن معه الأمر والنهى والتعذيب والإثابة . ومن أنكر بهذا خلقه فتعلقه بهذا النوع خيال ، وحقه أن ينظر الوجه الذى به يعرف خلق الأشياء ، فإن أمكن تحقيقه فالإنكار بهذا النوع إنما هو جهل بالحكمة . وعلى ذلك كان أول ما جبل عليه فيعلم إن خضع للمكرم به إن شاء الله ، وإن لم يمكن تسقط المسألة ، ويفضل الذي عارض كله ، ولا قوة إلا بالله به
And whoever was ignorant and from [?] the book of Tawhid [?] blameworthy, and it is from this aspect truth and wisdom, and the action from the perspective of the servant is foolishness and injustice, that aspect is ugly and disobedience. Do you not see that whoever knows the act of the disbeliever as it is in his view, if he informs of it, he is a liar, but whoever knows it as it is in its reality, he is knowing and wise, and if he informs of it, he is truthful. So similarly, God created that and made it as it is, and the act of the servant [is not?]. And according to the statement of whoever makes the creation of a thing other than it, it has no meaning; because the act of God in reality is not unbelief nor injustice nor foolishness, nor is that which came from the servant of humility and lowliness and obedience and disobedience, and there is no power except with God. Then he opposes the naming of other than the one who created death and the states of creation is more deserving than the one who created, and it is in summary named that He is the creator of that, so whatever he says in that, it is an answer to him in the first: and the principle is that it is established that the servant has an act in reality, and that he chooses for it, and that he prefers things in his view and loves them, and that the creation of that did not push him to it, nor compel him, nor constrain him to it, so the existence of that and the existence of His knowledge of it and His report about it and its affirmation in the Preserved Tablet and the requirement of His enmity for the time of his act and His naming it with what He named, since He did not constrain him to his act nor compel him to it, is consistent with command and prohibition and punishment and reward. And whoever denies this about His creation and clings to this type is an illusion, and his duty is to consider the aspect by which the creation of things is known, for if its verification is possible, then denial in this manner is ignorance of wisdom. And upon that was the first thing he was created with, so that he knows if he submits to the honored one by it if God wills, and if it is not possible, the question falls, and the one who opposes all of that is preferred, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 842

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing the two aspects of human actions: as divine creation and as human acquisition. Maturidi begins by stating that an action considered from the aspect of God's creation is true and wise, but from the aspect of the servant it may be foolishness and sin. He illustrates with the example of knowing the disbeliever's act: if one reports it as the disbeliever sees it, that report is false; but if one reports it as it really is (i.e., as God's creation), that report is true. Therefore, God's creation of the act is just, while the servant's act is subject to moral judgment. He then addresses those who deny that the servant has a real act, arguing that such a denial renders the distinction meaningless. Instead, it is established that the servant has a real act and chooses it, and that God's creation does not compel him. Hence, divine command, prohibition, punishment, and reward are consistent with this reality. Those who deny this and cling to objections are following an illusion and fail to understand the wisdom behind the divine decree. Maturidi concludes that this principle is the foundational disposition upon which humans are created.

Key Terms
فعل
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The denial of the servant's real act is a valid theological position.
Correction: Maturidi calls such denial an illusion and ignorance of wisdom, affirming the reality of human acquisition.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi call the denial of the servant's real act?
A) Wisdom.
B) An illusion.
C) Truth.
D) Command.

Key Takeaway
Denying the servant's acquisition is an illusion rooted in ignorance of the wisdom behind divine creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself feeling proud of a good deed as if you alone accomplished it? How does Maturidi's warning that such denial is an illusion challenge your inner sense of self-sufficiency, and what concrete step can you take today to remember God's creation in your actions?
?
When you sin, do you sometimes feel that your action was entirely your own and therefore you are utterly guilty? Or do you recognize that both your act and its creation come from God, yet you are still accountable? How does this lesson's teaching on acquisition reshape your understanding of repentance and your next step toward God?
?
Consider a moment you dismissed the role of God in your daily choices, perhaps without even noticing. Maturidi says that denial is 'ignorance of wisdom.' What specific area of your life (work, relationships, habits) have you been most reluctant to attribute to God's creation, and how will you deliberately acknowledge His hand in it starting today?

The Objections Against God Creating All Actions
Maturidi lists objections to universal divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objections raised by the Qadariyya and Mu'tazila against the doctrine that God creates all actions, including human acts.

Core Idea
If God creates everything, He would be praised for evil—but that cannot be.

Maturidi begins by listing the arguments of those who deny that God creates all actions. These objectors argue that if God were the creator of everything, including human actions, then He would be praised for creating evil acts, which is absurd. They also point to specific scriptural evidence and draw a comparison to the Magians. This lesson presents these objections as Maturidi records them.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the literal translation. Identify the two main objections mentioned.
The objections are introduced with 'من ذلك' and 'والثاني'.
2
Examine the scriptural claim
Notice that the objectors say they have specified evidence from verses. Consider how they might be interpreting the Quran.
3
Reflect on the hadith connection
The passage ends with the hadith linking Qadariyya to Magians. Think about why this comparison is made.
This sets up Maturidi's response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر أسئلة : من ذلك قوله : خالق كل شيء وأعمال العباد أشياء ، فزعم أن ذا امتداح ، وليس ذلك فى شتم نفسه ولا فى الكفر به ولا في فعل الأنبياء والثانى أنه عاب الكفر وعذب عليه ، ولا يجوز ذلك على ما يفعله . وقال : خصصنا أيضا بما تلونا من الآيات ، ودليل ما لم يدخل في ذلك ، وهو شيء ، مع وجود آيات ذلك مخرجها ، وهن خاصة . وبعد، فإن القبائح لم تذكرا فى هذا على رسول الله ، وانما ذكر في الجواهر [۱۲۸ ] المورثة . وقال : بل قول المجوس : إن الله أراد شيئا مما هي محرمة في الإسلام، ولذلك قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة قال الشيخ رحمه الله : نقول وبالله التوفيق إذ ثبت أن الآية بحق الامتداح كان في خروج شيء من الكائنات امتداح بغير الذى له ، أو بما يشاركه فيه كل ضعيف ؛ لأنه لو أراد كلية الأشياء ، ولم يكن خلقها ، فامتدح بغير الذي له ، وذلك كذب ، وفى إخراج البعض مساواة غيره فى أنه صانع كل شيء ، يريد ما لا صنع لغيره فيه ، وذلك فاسد مع ما لو جاز ذلك على الصرف إلى غير الذي لغير فعل ليجوز أن يُقال : ليس بخالق شيء ، على أنه ليس بخالق ما هو فعل لغيره ، فاذ كان وصفا له بالذم والعبودة ثبت أن الأول وصف له بالمدح والربوبية ، وفى التخصيص إيجاب الأول . وأيضا أنه قال : هو رب كل شيء ، وإله كل شيء ، وهو على كل شيء وكيل ، ولم يجز إخراج شيء عن ذلك ، وإن كان لا يليق القول به على التخصيص لقبح نحو أن يقال : رب الخبائب وإله القبائح ووكيل الشياطين وابليس ، وقائم على كل نتن وقذر ، فمثله الأول : وإن كان يقبح على التخصيص فى أشياء من حيث التسمية . وبهذا الوجه الذي قال شهدت المجوس والزنادقة أن الله تعالى لم يخلق مؤذيا ولا فسادا ، ولا أمات وليا ولا قوني عدواً ، ولا أبقى الشياطين ، ولا أعطى من يعلم أنه يشتمه ويصد طاعته أحدا ، لقوة ذكرنا ذلك ليعلموا أن أصل الاعتزال مقدر عن ذلك ؛ إذ إليه فزعهم عند مخالفتهم المفهوم من القرآن ، ومما جرى عليه قول الإسلام. ولذلك قال رسول الله عليه السلام : القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة . ولو جاز خروج شيء من أن يكون يكون هو من أسماء له خالقا لجاز مثله عن الملك والربوبية ونحو ذلك الامتداح ، فيبطل أن يكون له مدح بشيء ؛ لما فى كل شيء له شركاء في حقيقة معناه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
Then he mentioned questions: among that is his statement: 'Creator of everything, and the actions of servants are things', so he claimed that this is praise, but that is not in reviling oneself nor in disbelief in Him nor in the acts of the prophets. And the second: that He blamed unbelief and punished it, and that is not permissible for what He does. And he said: we also have specified by what we recited of the verses, and evidence of what does not enter into that, and it is a thing, while there are verses for that, its extraction, and they are specific. And after that, the ugly deeds were not mentioned in this concerning the Messenger of God, but rather mentioned in the jewels [128] the inheritance. And he said: rather the statement of the Magians: that God willed something from what is forbidden in Islam, and therefore the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' The Sheikh, may God have mercy on him, said: we say, and with God is success: since it is established that the verse is by right of praise, if any of the existents came out, it would be praise for other than the one to whom it belongs, or for what every weakling shares with him in it. Because if He willed all things and had not created them, then He would be praised for what is not His, and that is falsehood. And in bringing out some, it is equating others with Him in that He is the maker of everything, meaning that which no other has a hand in, and that is corrupt. Moreover, if that were permissible for diverting to other than the one for whom the act is, then it would be permissible to say: He is not the creator of anything, on the basis that He is not the creator of what is the act of another. Since it would be a description of Him with blame and servitude, it is established that the first is a description of Him with praise and lordship, and in specification is the affirmation of the first. Also, He said: He is the Lord of everything, and the God of everything, and He is over everything a guardian, and it is not permissible to exclude anything from that, even if it is inappropriate to say it with specification due to ugliness, like saying: Lord of impurities, God of abominations, guardian of devils and Iblis, and standing over every filth and dirt. So the first is similar to this, even if it is ugly when specified for some things in terms of naming. And by this aspect, the Magians and heretics testified that God Most High did not create anything harmful nor corruption, nor did He cause a saint to die nor raise an enemy, nor did He preserve the devils, nor did He give to anyone whom He knows will revile Him and divert His obedience, due to the strength of what we mentioned, so that they may know that the root of Mu'tazilism is derived from that; for to it they flee when they contradict the understanding of the Qur'an and what the statement of Islam has proceeded upon. Therefore the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' And if it were permissible for anything to come out of being a creator for Him, then the like would be permissible concerning the kingdom and lordship and similar praise, so that no praise would be established for Him for anything; because in everything there are partners for Him in the reality of its meaning, and there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 842

Commentary
This passage is an objection-answer sequence. Maturidi first lists objections raised against the doctrine that God is the creator of all things, including human actions. The objectors argue that if God is the creator of everything, then describing Him as 'Creator of all things' would be praise, but such praise would include blameworthy acts. They also argue that God cannot punish unbelief if He creates it. They claim to have scriptural evidence for their position. Maturidi then attributes similar views to the Magians and cites the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' In his response, Maturidi argues that if the verse were praise only for the one who creates all things, then limiting creation to some things would be praise for a quality shared by others, which is false. Furthermore, if one could exclude some things from God's creation, one could also say He is not the creator of anything, leading to absurdity. He explains that although it would be inappropriate to specify certain ugly things when describing God (e.g., 'Lord of impurities'), the general description 'Creator of everything' is valid because the ugliness is in the specific object, not in the creative act. He then states that the Magians and heretics deny that God creates harmful things, and this is the origin of Mu'tazilism. The hadith confirms this link. Finally, he concludes that if any existent could be excluded from God's creation, then His praise as 'Creator of everything' would be invalid because every existent would have partners in its meaning.

Key Terms
خالق (Creator)
امتداح (praise)
مجوس (Magians)
قدرية (Qadariyya)
اعتزال (Mu'tazilism)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if God creates all actions, He would be responsible for evil and cannot justly punish.
Correction: Maturidi will later show that this objection misunderstands the nature of divine praise and the logic of creation.

Checkpoint
Which group did the Prophet liken to the Magians?
A) Mu'tazila
B) Qadariyya
C) Ash'aris
D) Maturidis

Key Takeaway
The opponents argue that universal creation leads to praising God for evil and contradicts His justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see or experience evil, do you ever question whether God truly controls all things? How does this passage challenge you to reaffirm your belief that everything—even suffering—is from Him?
?
The Qadariyya argued that if God creates actions, He cannot justly punish. Have you ever secretly harbored the thought that God's decree is unfair? What would it cost you to fully submit to His wisdom?
?
The Prophet called those who deny divine creation of actions 'Magians of this community.' In what subtle ways do you separate God from certain aspects of your life, acting as if they are outside His control? How can you repent from this today?

Divine Decree
advanced

Maturidi's Refutation: The Necessity of Universal Creation
Maturidi refutes objections with logical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that if God is not the creator of everything, then He could not be praised as Creator at all.

Core Idea
If you exclude any thing from God's creation, He is no longer Creator of all.

Maturidi now responds to the objections. He shows that the very logic of praise requires that God be the creator of every existent. If some things were not created by Him, then He would be praised for something that is not genuinely His, or would have partners in creation—both are false. This lesson follows his reasoning and its implications for the Qadariyya.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's response
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Maturidi begins with a conditional argument about praise.
His argument is structured in a logical chain.
2
Understand the praise argument
Maturidi argues that if some existents were not created by God, then the verse 'Creator of everything' would be praise for a quality shared with others or for something not His. This is false.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Analyze the lordship analogy
He extends the same logic to lordship and guardianship: if we exclude ugly things, it would be inappropriate to say 'Lord of impurities', but the general description remains valid.
The inappropriateness is in the specific object, not in the creative act.
4
Connect to Mu'tazilism
Maturidi concludes that the root of Mu'tazilism is derived from the Magian denial that God creates harmful things. The hadith confirms this.
This reinforces the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is an objection-answer sequence. Maturidi first lists objections raised against the doctrine that God is the creator of all things, including human actions. The objectors argue that if God is the creator of everything, then describing Him as 'Creator of all things' would be praise, but such praise would include blameworthy acts. They also argue that God cannot punish unbelief if He creates it. They claim to have scriptural evidence for their position. Maturidi then attributes similar views to the Magians and cites the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' In his response, Maturidi argues that if the verse were praise only for the one who creates all things, then limiting creation to some things would be praise for a quality shared by others, which is false. Furthermore, if one could exclude some things from God's creation, one could also say He is not the creator of anything, leading to absurdity. He explains that although it would be inappropriate to specify certain ugly things when describing God (e.g., 'Lord of impurities'), the general description 'Creator of everything' is valid because the ugliness is in the specific object, not in the creative act. He then states that the Magians and heretics deny that God creates harmful things, and this is the origin of Mu'tazilism. The hadith confirms this link. Finally, he concludes that if any existent could be excluded from God's creation, then His praise as 'Creator of everything' would be invalid because every existent would have partners in its meaning.

Key Terms
خالق (Creator)
رب (Lord)
وكيل (Guardian)
مجوس (Magians)
قدرية (Qadariyya)
اعتزال (Mu'tazilism)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what would happen if it were permissible to exclude some things from God's creation?
A) He would still be praised as Creator of all.
B) It would lead to denying that He is the creator of anything.
C) The Magians would be correct.
D) The Qadariyya would be proven wrong.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi proves that universal creation is necessary for God to be praised as Creator of all and that limiting creation leads to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation you find ugly or painful—like a personal failure or a tragedy—do you instinctively wish to separate that event from God's will? How does Maturidi's argument challenge your heart to submit even the parts of life you dislike under His lordship? Will you today consciously affirm, 'My Lord is Lord over this too,' and mean it in your prayer?
?
The Magians and Qadariyya tried to protect God's honor by denying He creates evil, but Maturidi shows this actually diminishes His praise. Have you ever avoided attributing a trial to God because it felt disrespectful? How does this teaching force you to reconsider your own hidden assumptions about God's role in the difficult parts of your life? Commit to thanking Him for one hardship this week as part of His perfect creation.
?
If every existent, including your own sins and failures, is created by God, then your pride (which tries to claim that your good deeds are solely yours) and your despair (which blames God for your evil) are both refuted. Examine your heart: which of these two—pride or despair—do you use to escape full surrender to His absolute lordship? What specific step will you take today to acknowledge that He is the Creator of everything in your story, the hard as well as the easy?

Why the Qadariyya Are Worse Than the Magians
The author compares Qadariyya to Magians to expose their inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi argues that the Qadariyya are worse than the Magians, focusing on their inconsistency in denying Allah's creation of all actions.

Core Idea
Denying Allah’s creation of good is worse than attributing evil to another source.

Imam Maturidi presents a striking comparison: the Magians, who believed in two creators, are actually more consistent in honoring Allah than the Qadariyya, who claim to defend Allah’s justice but end up denying His creation of all actions. This lesson unpacks that argument and exposes the logical flaw in the Qadari position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the force of the comparison and the example of inconsistency.
Notice how the author uses the Magians as a foil to highlight the Qadariyya's error.
2
Understand the comparison
The author compares the Magians' view (good from Allah, evil from another principle) with the Qadariyya's view (denying Allah creates any action). Which is more respectful of Allah?
The Magians at least attribute good to Allah, while the Qadariyya deny even good actions from Allah.
3
Identify the inconsistency
The Qadariyya claim in general that Allah is the Lord of everything, but when asked about specific evil actions, they refuse to attribute them to Allah. This is self-contradictory.
The author uses the analogy of 'Allah is everywhere' but not in filthy places to illustrate this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم كان قول المجوس خيرا من قول القدرية عند التحصيل؛ لأنهم نزهوا الله عز وجل عن قول الشر وما يُذم الفاعل عليه وحققوا له فعل الخير وما يحمد عليه، ثم القدرية بالوجه الذى أنكر المجوس صرفوا الآية عن المفهوم تسترا، وأبطلوا عنه أيضا خلق كل شيء يحمد عليه من الخيرات، ونسأل الله العصمة. ثم من حيدهم أن سئل عن حكم الآية فأعرض عن ذلك واشتغل في الإجابة عن نوع الأفعال، وحقيقته أن يقول به فى الجملة، وعند التفسير فيما يقبح لا يقول كما يقول: الله فى كل مكان، فإذا سئل عنه فى الحشوش والأمكنة القذرة أبى ذلك، ثم هو رب كل شيء وإله كل شيء، ثم عند التفسير فيما يقبح يأبى إلا أنه لما يصير بحيث ذلك الإطلاق يدفع أصله، فمثله ما نحن فيه، والله الموفق.
Then the statement of the Magians is better than the statement of the Qadariyya upon analysis; because they (Magians) declared Allah free from (attributing to Him) the saying of evil and what the doer is blamed for, and they affirmed for Him the doing of good and what He is praised for. Then the Qadariyya, in the way that the Magians rejected, distorted the verse from its understood meaning as a cover, and also nullified for Him the creation of everything praised of good deeds. And we ask Allah for protection. Then among their evasions: if asked about the ruling of the verse, they turn away and occupy themselves in answering about the type of actions. And the reality is that they affirm it in general, but in interpretation concerning what is ugly they do not affirm, just as they say: 'Allah is in every place'. If asked about privies and filthy places, they refuse that. Then He is the Lord of everything and the God of everything, yet in interpretation concerning what is ugly they refuse, except that when it comes to [a situation] where that absolute statement would refute their principle, so similar is what we are in. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 846

Commentary
This passage is a comparison and refutation of the Qadariyya. The author argues that the Magians (dualists) are actually better than the Qadariyya because the Magians at least attribute only good to Allah and evil to another principle, thus preserving Allah's transcendence from evil. The Qadariyya, on the other hand, distort the clear meaning of the Qur'anic verses to deny that Allah creates any action—including good actions—thereby stripping Allah of His attribute of creation with respect to actions. The author then points out their inconsistency: they claim that Allah is the Lord of everything in a general sense, but when asked about specific ugly actions, they refuse to attribute their creation to Allah. This is analogous to someone who says 'Allah is everywhere' but denies He is in filthy places. The same self-contradiction applies here: they affirm the general principle but deny its implications when pressed.

Key Terms

القدرية
الشر
الخير
الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya are better than the Magians because they avoid attributing evil to Allah.
Correction: The author argues the opposite: the Magians are better because they at least attribute good to Allah, while the Qadariyya deny Allah's creation of all actions, including good.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the statement of the Magians is better than that of the Qadariyya?

D) The Magians worship fire, which is less harmful than the Qadariyya's innovations.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya are worse than the Magians because they deny Allah’s creation of good actions while claiming He is Lord of everything, revealing a fundamental inconsistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Refuting the Qadariyya's Interpretation: Actions are Created
Maturidi refutes Qadariyya using verse analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the claim that the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refers only to idols, and instead proves that actions are created.

Core Idea
The verse's apparent meaning is action creation; parallels prove blame is for the act.

The Qadariyya claimed that the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refers to the idols they carved, not to human actions. Imam Maturidi dismantles this interpretation by analyzing the verse's apparent meaning and the logic of parallel verses. This lesson walks through his key arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's claim
The Qadariyya cite the verse and parallel texts (37:95 'Do you worship what you carve?' and 7:117 'It swallows what they fake') to argue that 'what you do' means the carved idols, not actions.
2
Follow the author's refutation
Maturidi makes three points: (1) The apparent meaning is creation of action, and cannot be diverted without evidence. (2) In the parallels, blame is for the act of carving/faking, not the object. (3) If the verse meant idols, they would be 'ma'mul' (objects), but the verse does not say that.
Focus on the logical flow.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The verse establishes that actions are created by Allah, because they are blamed and worshipped, and the structure of the verse supports action creation.
The conclusion is that human actions are created, refuting the Qadariyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج لخصمه بقوله: وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُم وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ، قال: يريد به، كقوله: ( أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحَتُونَ )، وكقوله: تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق ظاهر الآية ذكر خلق العمل، فلم يجز صرف ذلك إلى غيره إلا بالبيان، مع ما فى جميع ما ذكر نحتهم[؟] داخل، وكذلك إفكهم ما ذكر وبه عوبوا لا بذلك الشيء حيث فعلوا ثم عبدوا، فكأنهم عبدوا فعلهم فمثله ما نحن فيه. أيضا أنه لو شرح بالآية آلهتهم ذكر معمولا، فإذا لم يكن الله خلق العمل لم يجز له القول بخلقه معمولا؛ إذ ليس هو كذلك مخلوقا، فثبت أن العمل مخلوق، ليعبدوا مخلوقا معمولا كما ذكر: ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then he argued for his opponent with His statement: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' He said: He intends by it, like His statement: 'Do you worship what you carve?' and like His statement: 'It swallows what they fake.' The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, said: We say, and with Allah is success: The apparent meaning of the verse mentions the creation of the action, so it is not permissible to divert that to other than it except with evidence. Moreover, in all that was mentioned, their carving is included, and likewise their faking which was mentioned, and they were blamed for it not for that thing where they did it and then worshipped. So it is as if they worshipped their own action, so similar is what we are in. Also, if he had interpreted the verse [as referring to] their deities, they would be mentioned as objects (ma'mul). So if Allah had not created the action, it would not be permissible for him to say that He created it as an object; since it is not created in that way. So it is established that the action is created, so that they worship a created object as mentioned: and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 846

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from the Qadariyya and the author's response. The opponents cite the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) but claim it refers to the idols they carve, not to human actions. They support this by parallel verses like 'Do you worship what you carve?' (37:95) and 'It swallows what they fake' (7:117). The author refutes this by pointing out: (1) The apparent meaning of the verse is the creation of the action itself, and it cannot be diverted without proof. (2) In the parallel verses, the objects carved or faked are included, but the blame is for the act of carving/faking, not for the object. So the worship is of the action itself. (3) If the verse meant their deities, those deities would be mentioned as 'ma'mul' (things worked upon), but they are not. Moreover, if Allah did not create the action, the verse would not say He created it as a 'ma'mul'. Thus the verse proves that actions are created.

Key Terms
العمل
المعمول
الخلق
عبادة
نحت
إفك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refers to the idols that the polytheists carved, not to human actions.
Correction: The verse's apparent meaning is the creation of action, and it cannot be diverted without evidence. Parallel verses show blame is for the act, not the object.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Imam Maturidi gives for rejecting the interpretation that 'what you do' refers to idols?
A) The verse was abrogated.
B) The apparent meaning is the creation of action, and the parallel verses show blame is for the act.
C) The grammar of the verse forces it to mean actions.
D) The Qadariyya are unreliable narrators.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' proves that human actions are created by Allah, as the apparent meaning and parallel verses demonstrate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you truly believe that every action you take — even your sins — is created by Allah? How does that affect the way you view your own responsibility and need for repentance?

When you read the verse 'Allah created you and what you do,' does it make you feel helpless or does it deepen your trust in Allah's control over all affairs? Be honest: which feeling dominates your heart, and why?
?
If you were to apply the Qadariyya logic to your own life, would you be more likely to excuse your wrongdoings as 'not created by Allah' and thus less serious? How does this lesson challenge you to take full responsibility for your actions while still affirming Allah's sovereignty?

Refuting the Qadariyya's Misuse of the Bahira Verse
Refutation of Qadariyya misuse of Bahira verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qadariyya misused the verse about Bahira to deny Allah's creation of actions, and the refutation based on linguistic and theological precision.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya confuse the creation of entities with the creation of actions.

The Qadariyya, in their attempts to deny that Allah creates human actions, resorted to misinterpreting Quranic verses. One such verse is about pre-Islamic practices concerning livestock known as Bahira. This lesson unpacks their flawed argument and the author's incisive refutation, showing how careful attention to language and theology exposes their error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: Bahira, a'yan (entities), af'al (actions).
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the Qadariyya argument
The Qadariyya cite verse 5:103. What do they claim it proves? How do they interpret 'ja'ala'?
They claim that 'Allah has not made a Bahira' negates creation of actions.
3
Understand the refutation
The author points out that the verse speaks about specific entities (a'yan), not actions. The denial is about a specific designation, not creation. How does the author argue this?
The entities are created, but the verse denies a specific status.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that this shows the Qadariyya reject Allah's reports and don't rely on His decree. How does this reveal their flawed methodology?
They twist the text to fit their preconceived theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من عِظَم سفههم أن احتجوا بقوله تعالى: مَا جَعَلَ الله مِنْ بُحَيْرَ وتلك أسماء تلك الأعيان فى نفى خلق الأعمال بقوله: ما جعل كذا تلك الأعيان لا الأفعال، وهن مخلوقات لا شك، ثم يرد فما ذكر العمل بالخلق إلى حقيقة الأعيان ليدفع خلق الأفعال، فهذا يبين أن رأيهم أن لا يقبلوا عن الله خبره، ولا يرجو فى أمر إلى تدبيره، والله أسأل العصمة
Then from the magnitude of their foolishness: they argued with His statement, exalted: 'Allah has not made a Bahira' and those are names of those entities (a'yan) in negating the creation of actions by His statement: 'He did not make' — those entities, not the actions, and they are created without doubt. Then they refer what was mentioned of action by creation to the reality of the entity to repulse the creation of actions. This shows that their opinion is that they do not accept Allah's report, nor do they rely in any matter on His management. And Allah I ask for protection.
Source pages p. 847

Commentary
This passage refutes another argument of the Qadariyya. They cite the verse 'Allah has not made a Bahira' (5:103), which mentions certain pre-Islamic practices concerning livestock, to argue that Allah does not create actions. The author points out that the verse talks about specific entities (a'yan), not actions. These entities are indeed created by Allah, but the verse denies that Allah made them as Bahira — a specific designation, not the creation of the act of designating. The Qadariyya twist the text: they take the word 'make' (ja'ala) and apply it to actions, but the verse's objects are physical entities. The author concludes that this reveals their rejection of Allah's reports and their lack of reliance on His decree.

Key Terms
البحيرة
الأعيان
الأفعال
الخلق
الجعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Allah has not made a Bahira' proves that Allah does not create human actions.
Correction: The verse negates a specific designation (being a Bahira) for animals, not the act of creating. The entities (a'yan) are created, but the verse denies a particular status.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Qadariyya's error in using the verse about Bahira?
A) They misquote the verse.
B) They treat the denial of making a specific entity as a denial of creating actions.
C) They ignore that the verse is abrogated.
D) They think Bahira refers to actions.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya's misuse of the Bahira verse reveals their flawed methodology of twisting the Quranic text to deny Allah's creation of actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Qadariyya twisted the Quran to fit their preconceived denial of divine decree. Think of an area in your life where you have read the Quran or listened to a teaching but twisted it to justify your own desires. What is one specific verse you have misinterpreted? How will you correct that today?
?
The author says the Qadariyya 'do not accept Allah's report, nor do they rely in any matter on His management.' Honestly, do you truly rely on Allah's management in your daily affairs, or do you try to control everything yourself? What would it look like for you to surrender a specific situation to Him right now?
?
Seeking protection from misguidance is a prayer of the author. When was the last time you sincerely asked Allah to protect you from misunderstanding His book? Set a reminder to include this in your daily supplication from today.

Refuting the Qadariyya on Similarity of Actions
Maturidi refutes Qadariyya on similarity of actions using verse on partners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi refutation of the Qadariyya argument that if human actions are created they would be similar to Allah's creation, and how the verse about 'partners who create as He creates' is correctly interpreted.

Core Idea
Human actions differ from Allah's creation in essence and quality; mere origination does not imply equality.

In this passage, Imam al-Maturidi addresses a final objection from the Qadariyya. They argue that if Allah creates human actions, then those actions would be like Allah's creation, leading to shirk. The Imam refutes this by distinguishing divine and human actions in kind and quality, and by clarifying the true meaning of the Qur'anic verse they misuse.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial response
Read the first part of the Arabic passage where the Qadariyya cite the verse and the author responds with 'معاذ الله'. Notice the stark contrast in the description of human vs. divine actions.
The author immediately rejects any similarity in quality.
2
Analyze the distinction in aspect (جهة) and meaning
Examine the sentences discussing الحدث (origination) and how similarity in the general fact of coming into existence does not imply equality due to different aspects and meanings.
The author uses the analogy of knowledge and power to illustrate difference in meaning.
3
Understand the Jahmi objection and the author's criticism
Read the part about Jahm's view and the author's surprise that the Qadariyya use the term 'originating' without applying the full reality of action to themselves.
This shows the inconsistency in their argument.
4
Grasp the final interpretation of the verse
Study the concluding statement by the jurist: the verse negates that anyone creates like Allah's unique creation, and it actually excuses the polytheists' worship had there been such creators.
Thus the verse cannot be used to deny that human actions are created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: واحتجوا أيضا بقوله: أَمْ جَعَلُوا لِلهِ شُرَكَاءَ خَلَقُوا كَخِلْقِه، إنه على قولكم تشبيه فعلكم خلقه، فقال: معاذ الله، بل فعلنا عبث وفساد وخضوع وذله، وفعله حكمة وصواب وتفضّل وتطول. قال: وليس من حيث الحدث، والحدث والخروج من العدم تشابه لاختلاف الجهة، كما لم يكن في عالم و قادر لاختلاف المعنى قال: وبعد، فإن فعلنا يخالف فعل الله لعينه، ثم الإيجاد والحدث معنى يوجب التشابه، وإنما يجوز ذلك فى الأعيان بما يحل فيها، مع ما يعارض بقول جهم حيث قال: في تحقيق الفعل تشابه، ثم قال: العجب من إلزامهم التسمية بالإحداث، ولم يلزموا أنفسهم فيما فعلوا فعل ربهم في الحقيقة قال الفقيه رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق أثبت الله تعالى التشابه من حيث الفعل حيث قال: خَلَقُوا كَخَلْقِهِ فَتَشَابَهَ الخَلْقُ عَلَيْهِم، نفى أن يكون من أحد خلق كخلقه، وأوجب لهم العذر في عبادتهم ما كانوا يعبدون لو كان كان منهم
He said: And they also argued with His statement: 'Or have they made for Allah partners who create as His creation?' — that according to your statement it would be a likeness of your action to His creation. So he said: Allah forbid! Rather, our action is frivolity, corruption, humility, and abasement, while His action is wisdom, correctness, favor, and bounty. He said: And [the likeness] is not from the aspect of origination (hadath); for origination and coming into existence from non-existence are similar due to difference of aspect, just as [two things] are not [similar] in being knowing and powerful due to difference of meaning. He said: Moreover, our action differs from Allah's action in its very essence; then bringing into existence and originating impart a meaning that necessitates similarity, and that is only permissible in entities (a'yan) by what inheres in them, besides what is contradicted by the statement of Jahm where he said: In the reality of the action there is similarity. Then he said: Strange is their requiring the naming with 'originating' while they do not require themselves to do the action of their Lord in reality. The jurist, may Allah have mercy on him, said: We say, and with Allah is success: Allah, exalted, affirmed similarity from the aspect of action where He said: 'They create as His creation, so the creation became similar to them' — He negated that anyone has a creation like His creation, and He made obligatory for them the excuse in their worship of what they worshipped, had it been from them.
Source pages p. 847

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes a final objection. The Qadariyya argue that if human actions are also created, then they would be similar to Allah's creation, leading to shirk. The author responds by distinguishing divine actions from human actions in quality and essence: human actions are flawed, while Allah's are perfect. The similarity is only in the general aspect of origination (hadath), but that does not imply equality because the quality and purpose differ. The author further mentions the Jahmi position that all actions are similar in being acts, then criticizes the Qadariyya for requiring the term 'originating' for humans but not applying it to themselves in reality. Finally, the author explains the true meaning of the verse: it negates that anyone can create like Allah's unique creation, so critics cannot use it to deny human actions being created; rather, it establishes that Allah's creation is unique and humans cannot replicate it.

Key Terms
التشابه
الفعل
الخَلق
الإحداث
الجهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse about 'partners who create as He creates' proves that human actions cannot be created by Allah because that would make human actions similar to Allah's creation.
Correction: The verse only negates that any other being creates in the unique manner of Allah; it does not deny that Allah creates human actions. The author shows that the verse actually excuses polytheists' worship if their deities were creators, but since they are not, it does not apply to human actions.

Checkpoint
How does the author initially respond to the Qadariyya's claim that human actions would be similar to Allah's creation?
A) He agrees but says it is a mystery.
B) He distinguishes the quality and essence of human actions from divine actions, stating that similarity in mere origination does not imply equality.
C) He says the verse is not about actions.
D) He says human actions are not real.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya misuse of the verse is refuted by distinguishing the quality of actions and the unique nature of Allah's creation; human actions are created but in a completely different manner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act of worship, do you sometimes feel a sense of pride, as if you are 'creating' something independent? How does this lesson's description of your actions as 'frivolity and corruption' next to Allah's 'wisdom and correctness' humble that feeling? Will you begin each act of worship with a conscious acknowledgment that your deed is merely a created, lowly thing, and only Allah's grace makes it acceptable?
?
You just read that the mere fact of 'origination' does not make two actions alike. Have you ever secretly compared your good deeds to Allah's actions, thinking your charity or patience is somehow on the same level as His generosity or forbearance? How will you actively remind yourself of the vast difference in quality and essence between your acts and His?
?
The Qadariyya argued that if Allah creates your actions, then your actions resemble His creation—implying you become like a partner. Have you ever felt a similar discomfort: if Allah is in control of everything, do my choices really matter? This lesson shows that divine creation and human action differ in aspect and essence. How does this distinction free you from both arrogance (thinking you create independently) and despair (thinking your actions are meaningless)? What specific step will you take today to live out this balance?

Actions Are Created: Proof and Quranic Refutation
Maturidi proves actions are created and refutes a Quranic objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's proof that human actions are created and how the verse 'Allah has not made any Bahirah' is misused by those who deny this.

Core Idea
Actions are created; the verse about Bahirah refers to entities, not actions.

Imam al-Maturidi establishes a fundamental point: human actions are created by Allah. He then addresses an objection raised by opponents who cite a Quranic verse about 'Bahirah' (a specific camel) to argue against the creation of actions. Maturidi exposes their error by clarifying that the verse speaks of physical entities, not actions. This lesson unpacks his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the flow: first the assertion that actions are created, then the refutation of an objection using Quranic verse 5:103.
Pay attention to the key terms 'العمل مخلوق' and 'الأعيان'.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two main sections: (1) the proof that action is created, and (2) the refutation of the objection from the Bahirah verse. Note how Maturidi distinguishes between entities (أعيان) and actions (أفعال).
3
Understand the refutation logic
Maturidi points out that the verse 'ما جعل الله من بحيرة' refers to specific entities (like the Bahirah camel), not to human actions. Those entities are indeed created, so the verse does not negate the creation of actions. The opponents misuse the verse by misapplying it.
The opponents' fallacy is equating the ruling of entities with that of actions.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi ends by criticizing the opponents' attitude: they reject Allah's report (the Quran) and do not rely on His decree. This shows the importance of accepting divine revelation fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ليس هو كذلك مخلوقا، فثبت أن العمل مخلوق، ليعبدوا مخلوقا معمولا كما ذكر: ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم من عظم سفههم أن احتجوا بقوله تعالى: (ما جعل الله من بحيرة) [المائدة:103]، وتلك أسماء تلك الأعيان في نفي خلق الأعمال بقوله: ما جعل كذا تلك الأعيان لا الأفعال، وهن مخلوقات لا شك، ثم يرد فما ذكر العمل بالخلق إلى حقيقة الأعيان ليدفع خلق الأفعال، فهذا يبين أن رأيهم أن لا يقبلوا عن الله خبره، ولا يرجو في أمر إلى تدبيره، والله أسأل العصمة.
It is not that way created, so it is established that action is created, so that they worship a created thing made as mentioned: and there is no power except with Allah. Then from the greatness of their foolishness is that they argued with His saying: (Allah has not made any Bahirah) [5:103], and those are the names of those entities in denying the creation of actions by His saying: He did not make such those entities not actions, and they are created without doubt. Then he responds regarding what was mentioned of action with creation to the reality of entities in order to repel the creation of actions. This shows that their opinion is that they do not accept from Allah His report, nor do they hope in any matter to His management, and Allah I ask for protection.
Source pages p. 847

Commentary
This passage is a proof-and-refutation unit. The author first asserts that actions are created, then identifies the foolishness of those who use the verse about 'Bahirah' to deny that. He explains that the verse refers to specific physical entities (like the Bahirah camel) and not to human actions; those entities are indeed created, but the verse does not negate the creation of actions. The author concludes that this argument shows the opponents reject God's own report and do not rely on His decree.

Key Takeaway

The Wisdom Behind God's Creation of Disbelief
Al-Maturidi explains the wisdom behind God's creation of disbelief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind God's creation of disbelief and how it serves to guide people to tawhid.

Core Idea
God's creation of disbelief is a means of guidance, not approval.

Al-Maturidi begins by addressing a common objection: if God creates disbelief, how can it be good? He explains that the act of disbelief, though ugly, serves a greater purpose: it warns the witness about the consequences of sin and drives them to seek Allah's protection. This lesson unpacks that wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on wisdom
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand Al-Maturidi's explanation of why God creates disbelief.
2
Identify the purpose
Notice how the act of disbelief leads the witness to 'flee to Allah for protection' and 'be called to tawhid'.
3
Reflect on the benefits
The passage mentions that through this, one recognizes the folly and sin of the disbeliever, and comes to know Allah's name and consequences.
4
Understand the final point
The passage concludes that the act does not harm the Maker, affirming Allah's sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : فالأول يقال له في خلق فعل الكفر قبيحا ، وهو بذكر من عاينه عظيم فعله ، فيفزع إلى الله بالعصمة عنه بما يذكره من حدث الذي منه ، فيدعوه إلى التوحيد ، ثم يعرف به سفه من منه ذلك وفسقه ، وبه يعرف اسمه وعواقبه ، ثم يعرفه أنه لا يضر الصانع ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقوله : لا يخلقه لا عن أحد ، كلام من لا يعقل ما يقول وإلا فهو اسم لفعل العبد ، فكيف يكون ولا عبد ، وهذا لمن يقول التحرك هو زوال الجسم لا يخلقه دونه ، فيجب خلقه منه حكمة ، وعلى ذلك الأعراض وإمانة الخلق ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الأسقام لا يجوز أن يخلقها لا في أحد ولا أحد ، ثم لم يمنع تحقق الحكمة لها ، فمثله الذي ذكر ، والله الموفق .
Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The first is said to him: In creating the act of disbelief it is ugly, and it is by mentioning to the one who witnesses it the greatness of His action, so he flees to Allah for protection from it by what he recalls of the temporality from which it comes, so it calls him to tawhid, then through it he knows the folly and sin of the one from whom it comes, and through it he knows His name and consequences, then he knows that it does not harm the Maker, and there is no power except with Allah. And His saying: He does not create it from no one, is the speech of one who does not understand what he says; otherwise it is a name for the act of the servant, so how can it be without a servant? And this is for the one who says motion is the removal of the body, He does not create it without it, so its creation from Him is necessary by wisdom, and likewise the accidents and the trust of creation, and there is no power except with Allah. Then diseases cannot be created in anyone without anyone, then the attainment of wisdom for them is not prevented, so it is like what was mentioned, and Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 851

Commentary
This passage explains the wisdom behind God's creation of the act of disbelief: it serves as a deterrent for those who witness it, prompting them to seek refuge in Allah and turn to tawhid. It also exposes the folly of the disbeliever. Then it refutes the claim that God does not create the act of disbelief from no one; rather, the act is attributed to the servant, but its creation is from God. The passage also touches on motion and accidents, asserting that they are created by God. Finally, it returns to diseases, stating that they are also created with wisdom.

Key Terms

قبيح
العصمة
التوحيد
سفه
فسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think that if God creates disbelief, He approves of it.
Correction: The text shows that God creates disbelief for a wise purpose: to warn others and guide them to tawhid, not because He approves of it.

Checkpoint

A) To harm the disbeliever
B) To cause others to seek protection and turn to tawhid
C) To test the angels
D) To show God's power

Key Takeaway
God's creation of disbelief is part of His wise plan to guide believers and expose the folly of sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Denial of God's Creation of Human Acts
Al-Maturidi refutes the claim that God does not create human acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Maturidi's refutation of those who deny that God creates human acts, including motion and diseases.

Core Idea
Denying God's creation of acts is incoherent; acts are defined by the agent, and all things are created by God.

Al-Maturidi now turns to refute those who claim that God does not create human acts. He argues that such a statement is irrational because an act requires an agent. He then uses examples like motion and diseases to demonstrate that their creation must be attributed to God, and this does not negate wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic and translation of Al-Maturidi's counter-argument.
2
Understand the logical flaw
The claimant says 'He does not create it from no one' - but this is incoherent because the act is named after the servant; it cannot exist without a servant.
3
Examine the motion example
If motion is defined as the removal of the body, the one who says God does not create it is refuted; its creation from God is necessary by wisdom.
4
Consider diseases
Diseases cannot be created in anyone without anyone else; they are also created with wisdom.
5
Conclude the argument
Thus, all things, including human acts, are created by God with wisdom.

Source Text

Refuting the Objection on Human Action
Al-Maturidi refutes an objection about human action using Zayd's example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Maturidi refutes the objection that human action implies independence from God by distinguishing between power to act and the meaning of existence.

Core Idea
Power to act does not equal creation; the source of existence is God alone.

In this passage, al-Maturidi continues a debate about human action. An opponent argues that if humans create their actions by their own power, then Zayd's action would be independent of God. Al-Maturidi refutes this by showing that the power to act is not the same as the power to bring something into existence. Read the text carefully to see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the back-and-forth between the opponent and the author.
The phrase 'there is no power except with Allah' appears twice, emphasizing divine control.
2
Identify the opponent's objection
The opponent claims that if humans act by their power, then Zayd's action (like any human action) would be independent of God. Find where this objection is presented.
The objection is implicit: 'How did you act Zayd's action?' implies that Zayd's action is problematic.
3
Understand the reply
The reply distinguishes between Zayd not giving power over his action (so he did not create it) and God giving power over the meaning of existence (so God is the true creator). Grasp this key distinction.
The reply shows inconsistency in the opponent's position: they accept that Zayd does not create, but deny God's role in creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأجاب بالفعل ، وذلك فاسد ؛ لأنا لم نحقق لنا في فعلنا الوجه الذي هو وجه وجود الجسم وكونه ليلزمنا ذلك ، وهم قد حققوا فيلزمهم ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم قال : إذ ليس فعل زيد سوى فعل بقدرة ، وأنتم تفعلون بها ، كيف فعلتم فعل زيد ؟ قيل : لأن زيدا لا يقدرنا على فعله ، فلم يفعل ، والله قد أقدركم على المعنى الذي به كان الجسم ، فلزمكم ما قابلناكم به ، ولا قوة إلا بالله .
So he answered by action, and that is corrupt; because we have not verified for ourselves in our action the aspect that is the aspect of the existence of the body and its being, so that it would be incumbent upon us, but they have verified it, so it is incumbent upon them, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he said: Since Zayd's action is nothing but an action by power, and you act by it, how did you act Zayd's action? It was said: Because Zayd does not empower us over his action, so he did not act, and Allah has empowered you over the meaning by which the body existed, so what we presented to you became incumbment upon you, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 851

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on action. The opponent responds with an argument about human action: if humans act by their own power, how can Zayd's action be attributed to God? The reply distinguishes: Zayd does not give us power over his action, so he didn't act it; but God gave us power over the meaning by which the body exists, so the argument applies to Him. Thus the inconsistency in the opponent's position is exposed.

قدرة
زيد
وجه الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans create their actions independently by their own power.
Correction: The passage shows that the power to act is distinct from the power to bring into existence. God gives power over the meaning of existence, so He is the true creator.

B) Because Zayd does not give others power over his action

Key Takeaway
The distinction between power to act and power to bring into existence is crucial: only God has the power to create, while human power is derived and limited.
